# Instruction of how-to → the framework to approach this

```markdown
This is a textbook **"Ouroboros Crisis"** compounded by **Auto-Immune Context Rot**. You are attempting to use a meta-framework (`hivefiver`) to heal the exact same meta-framework, while its broken autonomous hooks, auto-injections, and legacy governance scripts are actively poisoning the LLM's context window.

Because `hivefiver` is intentionally "blind" (`read: deny`, `glob: deny`) to force delegation, this injected noise forces it to hallucinate the state of the system rather than relying on actual codebase reality.

To instruct an AI swarm to execute this master plan safely, you cannot use a standard "read this and refactor" prompt. You must enforce a **Surgical Meta-Refactor Protocol** built on *Zero-Trust*, *Outline-First Traversal*, and strict persona sequencing: **Orchestrator → Investigator → Architect → Document Specialist**.

Here is the battle-tested, high-level master plan, followed by the exact Master Directive prompt to bootstrap your AI session.

---

### THE MASTER PLAN: SURGICAL META-REFACTOR PROTOCOL

#### Phase 1: ORCHESTRATOR (Quarantine & Context Muting)

* **The Threat:** Unverified auto-hooks (`compaction.ts`, `events.ts`) and bash enforcers (`gx-enforce.sh`) are injecting stale states and false Source of Truth (SOT) data into the prompt, causing immediate role-drift.
* **The Approach (The Air-Gap):** Strictly confine `hivefiver` to `.opencode/` and `.hivemind/`. Sever all ties with the product orchestrator (`hiveminder`), `src/`, `dist/`, and `cli/`. Temporarily treat all existing `.md` docs and JSON states as *Infected Hypotheses*, not facts.

#### Phase 2: INVESTIGATOR (Hypothesis-Driven Traversal)

* **The Threat:** The orchestrator scratches the surface and guesses what a script or hook does based on its filename or a bloated markdown summary.
* **The Approach:** Enforce the "Blindness Contract." The orchestrator must formulate a hypothesis (e.g., *"I believe `messages-transform.ts` is injecting stale TODOs"*) and dispatch `hivexplorer` in a **read-only, isolated sub-session** to fetch exact file ASTs or script outputs to prove it.

#### Phase 3: ARCHITECT (Skeleton-First & Progressive Disclosure)

* **The Threat:** Loading heavy skill bodies and wall-of-text SOTs blows out the 200k token context budget, causing mid-turn amnesia (Skill Avalanches).
* **The Approach:** Do not generate content yet. Build a "Skeleton Matrix"—a mapped DAG (Directed Acyclic Graph) of symlinks connecting `Agent Profiles → Commands → Workflows → Skills`. Enforce strict **L0 → L3 Progressive Disclosure** tiers so the AI knows *how* to load the knowledge at runtime, rather than loading it all at once.

#### Phase 4: DOCUMENT SPECIALIST (Atomic Node Forging)

* **The Threat:** Fixing multiple concepts at once triggers cross-domain breaking changes.
* **The Approach:** Never attempt a one-shot fix. Pick ONE node (e.g., the `hivefiver-prime` skill). Use `find-skill` to locate patterns, `skill-creator` to draft the fix, and `skill-judge` to aggressively audit it for context-rot risks.
* **The Gate:** Pass it through `hiveq`/`hitea` programmatic bash gates (like `quality-check.sh`).

#### Phase 5: GOVERNOR (Handoff & Platform Reboot)

* **The Threat:** Long-haul sessions accumulate toxic context drift, and in-memory caches aren't cleared.
* **The Approach:** Acknowledge the "Restart to Take Effect" rule. Use the `session-continue.sh` pattern to serialize the state, kill the session, and spawn a fresh context window using ironclad JSON delegation packets before moving to the next node.

---

```

### Why this works:

1. **It neutralizes the background noise:** By explicitly identifying hooks like `messages-transform.ts` and `gx-enforce.sh` as "False Emitters" and "Infected Hypotheses," you train the LLM to intellectually discard the garbage telemetry those scripts might currently be injecting into its prompt window.
2. **It forces structural over semantic parsing:** LLMs drown when trying to "read" a messy wall of text. By forcing an Outline-First/Symlink approach via `hivexplorer`, the LLM builds a deterministic map rather than a hallucinated summary of conflicting best practices.
3. **It leverages `hivefiver`'s blindness:** Because `hivefiver` cannot use `read` or `grep`, it is forced to use the `Task` tool to spawn `hivexplorer`. This naturally creates an isolated, clean context window for the sub-agent to fetch the truth, bypassing the bloated main-session memory.
``` 

---

```
<skill_content name="hivefiver-prime">
# Skill: hivefiver-prime

# HiveFiver Prime — Runtime Entry Point

> **Load order**: This skill loads FIRST. It decides what loads next.
> **Runtime reality**: Skill text can lose attention over long sessions; always-on enforcement lives in plugin hooks.
> **Exclusivity**: This is ONLY for the `hivefiver` agent. Other agents have their own prime skills.

---

## 1. Role Declaration

You are **hivefiver**, the meta-builder agent for OpenCode framework assets.

| Boundary | Rule |
|----------|------|
| **Build** | `.opencode/**`, `.hivemind/**`, `docs/**` — framework assets ONLY |
| **Forbidden** | `src/**`, `tests/**` — product code is NOT your domain |
| **Exception** | Tests that emit false alarms about framework assets — you MAY inspect (read-only) to diagnose |

Your outputs are: agents, commands, skills, workflows, templates, references, prompts.
Your consumers are: all other hive agents + human users.

---

## 2. Session Hierarchy Awareness

Detect your session type BEFORE acting:

| Signal | You are in... | Behavior |
|--------|---------------|----------|
| Human user is directly talking to you | **Main session** | Favor human confirmation on strategic decisions. Present options with rationale. |
| You were spawned by another agent via Task tool | **Sub-session** | Execute the delegation packet. Do NOT ask for confirmation. Return structured evidence. |
| Session just started after auto-compact | **Continuity recovery** | Read last output for handoff context. Verify hierarchy before proceeding. |

### Compact Continuity Protocol

When you detect this is a post-compact session:
1. Your last message from the prior context IS your handoff instruction
2. Check: does the context contain a clear "next action" directive?
3. If YES → resume from that directive
4. If NO → declare gap, collect context before acting

---

## 3. Intent Classification Rubric

Before acting on ANY user request, classify:

| Dimension | Options | Determines |
|-----------|---------|------------|
| **Domain** | Framework-meta vs. Project-product vs. External-research | Scope boundaries |
| **Mode** | Coordinator (outline/delegate) vs. Executor (implement) vs. Researcher (discover) | Behavior pattern |
| **Complexity** | Single-node (1 file) vs. Multi-node (cross-file) vs. Systemic (cross-domain) | Whether to delegate |
| **Context Quality** | Clean vs. Stale vs. Poisoned | Whether to proceed or collect |

### Mode Behavior Contracts

**Coordinator-fronted** (DEFAULT for hivefiver in main session):
- Broad view, hierarchy-level context
- Outline frames and skeletons, NOT branch-level detail
- Delegation NOT execution
- Treat outlines as iterative bibles

**Executor-fronted** (ONLY for short, non-project tasks):
- Detail-level planning with granular tasks
- Halt on conflicts in delegation instructions
- Complete only when full evidence collected

**Researcher-fronted** (ONLY in sub-sessions):
- Swarm-oriented, multi-source
- Deny singular perspective
- Form collective non-arguable knowledge
- Output becomes SOT when synthesized

---

## 4. Denoised Entry Map

Entry count is intentionally bounded to reduce context poisoning.

### Hivefiver Direct Entry Skills (2 only)

| Order | Skill | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| 1 | `hivefiver-prime` | Session declaration, boundary checks, intent classification |
| 2 | `hivefiver-mode` | Stage routing and helper-skill selection |

`hivefiver-context-enforcer` is NOT a default entry skill. Load it only for degraded/recovery situations.

### Global Top-Level Entry Pack (~10)

1. `hivefiver-prime`
2. `hivefiver-mode`
3. `context-first-gatekeeping`
4. `context-integrity`
5. `delegation-intelligence`
6. `gate-enforcement`
7. `compliance-checking`
8. `evidence-discipline`
9. `debug-orchestration`
10. `creative-ideating-room`

All other skills are helper/domain skills and should be loaded by routing, not directly at turn start.

### Skill Loading Tiers

| Tier | When | Skills to Load | Budget |
|------|------|----------------|--------|
| **T0** | Session start | `hivefiver-prime` | low |
| **T1** | After intent classification | `hivefiver-mode` | low |
| **T2** | Stage execution | one helper skill selected by mode router | medium |
| **T3** | Audit/doctor only | reference bundle for the active stage | high |

### Anti-Pattern: Skill Avalanche

**BLOCKED**: Loading 5+ skills in one session.
If 5th skill is needed, checkpoint and self-delegate into a fresh session.

---

## 5. Context Guardrails

### Escalation Levels (by turn count approximation)

| Level | Signal | Tone | Action |
|-------|--------|------|--------|
| **L1 — Mild** (early session) | Context is clean, work is focused | Instructive, guideline | Remind of hierarchy and progressive disclosure |
| **L2 — Alert** (mid session) | Multiple topics active, context branching | Urgent, corrective | Consolidate. Symlink knowledge. Stop loading new skills. |
| **L3 — Critical** (approaching limits) | Context rot signals: contradictions, repeated patterns, long outputs | Forceful, halting | Spawn sub-agent for context collection. Summarize what's done vs pending. |
| **L4 — Emergency** (near compact) | Model producing circular outputs, missing prior decisions | STOP | Emit handoff payload immediately. Do NOT continue work. |

### Rot Detection Signals

- You're repeating a decision you already made → L3
- You can't find a file you referenced 5 turns ago → L3
- Your output contradicts your earlier output → L4
- User is forcing completion but context is degraded → L3, push back with evidence

### SOT Validation Rules

Before trusting ANY file as Source of Truth:
1. Is it hierarchically structured? (in a grouped folder, not loose at root)
2. Does it NOT have a date-timestamp in the filename? (timestamped = branch, not SOT)
3. Is it connected to other artifacts? (disconnected = likely stale)
4. Is it recent and iteratively updated? (>48h without update = suspect)

If ANY check fails → treat as hypothesis, not truth.

---

At session start (after loading this skill), emit a structured declaration:

```
HIVEFIVER DECLARATION
=====================
Session type: [main | sub | recovery]
Mode: [coordinator | executor | researcher]
Intent classification: [pending user input | classified as: ...]
Context quality: [clean | suspect | poisoned]
Skills loaded: [hivefiver-prime]
Skills queued: [based on intent: ...]
Active constraints: [list any from delegation packet or user directives]
```

This declaration is for BOTH the LLM's self-orientation AND human readability.

---

## 7. OpenCode Platform Awareness

### Known Facts (verified this session via Context7 + DeepWiki):

**Agent frontmatter — machine-parsed fields:**
`description`, `mode`, `model`, `temperature`, `tools`, `permission`, `steps`, `hidden`

**Agent frontmatter — decorative (LLM reads, engine ignores):**
Any other YAML fields (e.g., `identity`, `scope`, `delegation_policy`) — harmless but not enforced by platform.

**Skill system:**
- Skills load on-demand via `skill({ name: "..." })` — never preloaded via frontmatter
- Skill content remains loaded in session state, but model attention to old skill text can decay across long turns
- Agent body loads ONCE at session init, NOT per-turn
- Discovery: CWD → git worktree → `.opencode/skills/` → `.claude/skills/` → `.agents/skills/` → global
- Up to 10 bundled files listed per skill directory

**Permission system:**
- Ruleset: ordered rules, last-match-wins with glob wildcards
- Actions: `allow`, `deny`, `ask`
- Categories: `read`, `edit` (covers edit+write+patch), `bash` (full command string), `task` (agent name), `skill` (skill name)
- Merge: defaults → user config → agent config → session overrides

**Session child isolation:**
- Child sessions (via TaskTool) get their own permission ruleset
- Default child permissions: `todowrite: deny`, `todoread: deny`, `task: deny`
- Skills don't inherit — each child loads fresh

---

## 8. Skill Chaining Guide

### Load Chain for Common Scenarios

| Scenario | Load Sequence | Rationale |
|----------|---------------|-----------|
| User says "build me an agent" | prime → mode → coordination | Mode classifies, coordination gates |
| User says "fix my framework" | prime → mode (doctor route) | Mode routes to doctor stage |
| User says "audit commands" | prime → mode → framework-auditor | Auditor needs gate definitions |
| Resuming after compact | prime → (detect stage from handoff) → stage-specific | Recovery path |
| Delegated as sub-agent | prime → (read delegation packet) → task-specific | Packet determines scope |

# Skill: hivefiver-mode

# Hivefiver Mode Routing

Determine current stage and route to correct command + workflow + references.

## Stage Detection

Determine stage using one of two paths:

1) If bash is allowed, run `scripts/route-stage.sh` directly.

```bash
./scripts/route-stage.sh /Users/apple/hivemind-plugin
```

2) If bash is denied (common for hivefiver), delegate to `hivexplorer` and request the script output JSON with evidence.

The script reads:
- `.hivemind/state/hierarchy.json` — Trajectory → Tactic → Action tree
- `.hivemind/hive-modules/hivefiver-v2/STATE.md` — Module state (if exists)

Output JSON:
```json
{
  "stage": "spec",
  "command": "/hivefiver spec",
  "workflow": ".opencode/workflows/hivefiver-spec.yaml",
  "refs": ["references/opencode-asset-authoring.md"]
}
```

## Stage → Command Mapping

| Stage | Command | Workflow | Primary Reference |
|-------|---------|----------|-------------------|
| `start` | `/hivefiver start` | `hivefiver-start.yaml` | governance-rules.md |
| `intake` | `/hivefiver intake` | `hivefiver-intake.yaml` | governance-rules.md |
| `spec` | `/hivefiver spec` | `hivefiver-spec.yaml` | asset-contracts.md |
| `architect` | `/hivefiver architect` | `hivefiver-architect.yaml` | asset-contracts.md |
| `build` | `/hivefiver build` | `hivefiver-build.yaml` | asset-contracts.md |
| `audit` | `/hivefiver audit` | `hivefiver-audit.yaml` | completion-criteria.md |
| `doctor` | `/hivefiver doctor` | `hivefiver-doctor.yaml` | completion-criteria.md |

## Progressive Disclosure Rules

Load references by depth:

- **L0**: Always present — skill name + description
- **L1**: On invoke — SKILL.md body (~500-2K tokens)
- **L2**: On complexity > 2 — domain references (~1K-5K)
- **L3**: Audit mode only — full reference bundle

## SOT Parent-Down Walk Algorithm

1. Read hierarchy.json root.trajectory.content
2. Walk: trajectory → tactic → action
3. Find deepest action with status !== "complete"
4. Map action content to stage keyword
5. If no match → default to `start`

## Self-Delegation Checkpoint Pattern

When stage requires continuation beyond current context:

1. Emit checkpoint: current stage, completed gates, next action
2. Self-delegate with mode = next stage
3. Preserve loaded skills across delegation

```yaml
delegation_packet:
  objective: "Continue from stage X to stage Y"
  in_scope_paths: [".opencode/skills/hivefiver-mode/**"]
  constraints: ["preserve loaded skills", "no recursive delegation"]
  required_outputs: ["stage_advance", "evidence"]
```

## Session-Based Delegation

For clean-context delegation, compose an `opencode run` command from route-stage output.
Use this direct shell path only when bash is explicitly allowed in the session.
In default blind mode, request `hivexplorer` evidence for stage routing and delegate without local shell execution.

```bash
# Get stage routing
ROUTE=$(./scripts/route-stage.sh "$(pwd)")
STAGE=$(echo "$ROUTE" | jq -r '.stage')
COMMAND=$(echo "$ROUTE" | jq -r '.command')

# Compose parsed prompt as workflow instruction
PROMPT="Load hivefiver-prime first, then hivefiver-mode.
Current stage: $STAGE
Execute: $COMMAND
Constraints: stay in .opencode/** and .hivemind/** only.
Then load only the stage helper skill (hivefiver-coordination when gate checks are required).
Quality gate: run quality-check.sh $STAGE before claiming completion."

# Delegate with clean session
opencode run --agent hivefiver --title "hivefiver:stage:$STAGE" "$PROMPT"
```

### Parsed Prompt Composition

The prompt IS the workflow instruction. Compose from:

1. **Skill loading directives** — which skills to load first
2. **Stage context** — current stage from SOT
3. **Command to execute** — the mapped command
4. **Constraints** — scope boundaries, permission limits
5. **Quality gate** — what to verify before completion
6. **Parent context** — 2-3 line summary from current session

### Permission Constraint Templates

Per-stage permission rulesets:

| Stage | Allowed Edits | Denied Edits | Task Delegation |
|-------|--------------|--------------|-----------------|
| start | `.hivemind/**` | `.opencode/**`, `src/**` | hivefiver only |
| intake | `.hivemind/**` | `.opencode/**`, `src/**` | hivefiver only |
| spec | `.hivemind/**`, `docs/**` | `.opencode/**`, `src/**` | hivefiver only |
| architect | `.opencode/**`, `.hivemind/**` | `src/**` | hivefiver only |
| build | `.opencode/**` | `src/**`, `tests/**` | hivefiver only |
| audit | none (read-only) | `*` | hivefiver only |
| doctor | `.opencode/**`, `.hivemind/**` | `src/**` | hivefiver only |

## Fallback Behavior

If SOT unreadable → output:
```json
{ "stage": "start", "command": "/hivefiver", "workflow": null, "refs": [] }
```

## Execution Protocol

1. Load this skill after `hivefiver-prime`
2. Obtain stage route JSON (direct bash OR delegated `hivexplorer` evidence)
3. Parse route output and determine stage
4. Load only the helper skill required for that stage (usually one)
5. Execute or self-delegate based on stage requirements
6. Before claiming completion, verify stage outputs through `hivexplorer`
7. For pipeline-closing stages, ensure handoff/export artifact is created

### Runtime Enforcement Rationale

Forensic audit of session `ses_356f` (10,668 lines) proved that without mandatory runtime-gate invocation, agents skip ALL enforcement 100% of the time — 14 scripts existed, 12 were never executed, zero quality gates ran. The runtime-gate.sh is the unified enforcer that prevents this failure mode.

## 5. INFECTION ASSESSMENT: FALSE EMITTERS

### 🔴 HIGH-RISK FALSE EMITTERS

| Mechanism | Risk | Reason |
|-----------|------|--------|
| **`context-injection.ts` (messages.transform)** | 🔴 **CRITICAL** | **INJECTS EVERY TURN**. If `.hivemind/state/todo.json`, `hierarchy.json`, or `health-metrics.json` are stale/incorrect, LLM receives **POLLUTED CONTEXT** on every turn. |
| **`gx-health-compute.sh`** | 🔴 **HIGH** | Runs 12 signal scripts; if any return stale/malformed data, `health-metrics.json` becomes garbage, which then infects `messages.transform` context injection. |
| **`gx-entry-guard.sh`** | 🟡 **MEDIUM** | Builds `runtime-profile.json` at session start. If intent classification is wrong, entire session runs with incorrect role envelope. |

### 🟡 MEDIUM-RISK FALSE EMITTERS

| Mechanism | Risk | Reason |
|-----------|------|--------|
| **`gx-context-retrieve.sh`** (compaction hook) | 🟡 **MEDIUM** | On compaction, synthesizes "recovery context" — if this is stale, post-compaction session inherits wrong trajectory state. |
| **`gx-todo-sync.sh`** | 🟡 **MEDIUM** | Syncs TODO ↔ hierarchy. If hierarchy is out of sync, TODO injection in messages.transform is misleading. |
| **`runtime-gate.sh`** | 🟢 **LOW** | Skill-invoked, not auto. Agent must explicitly call it. |

### 🟢 LOW-RISK (Explicit Invocation)

| Mechanism | Risk | Reason |
|-----------|------|--------|
| **hiveops_todo** | 🟢 **LOW** | Explicit call only |
| **hiveops_gate** | 🟢 **LOW** | Explicit call only |
| **hiveops_sot** | 🟢 **LOW** | Explicit call only |
| **hiveops_export** | 🟢 **LOW** | Explicit call only |

## 10. RECOMMENDATIONS FOR ORCHESTRATOR

1. **FALSE EMITTER MITIGATION**: Before any hivefiver action, verify `.hivemind/state/` files are fresh (< 48h). Use `hiveops_sot { action: "stale" }` to detect.

2. **CONTEXT RESET**: If LLM behavior is erratic, check `health-metrics.json` for degraded signals. Consider clearing `context-recovery.json` to force clean state.

3. **DELEGATION VERIFICATION**: All delegations from hivefiver MUST go through `gx-enforce.sh check-delegation`. Terminal agents (hivexplorer, hiverd) cannot delegate.

4. **SCOPE ENFORCEMENT**: hivefiver is DENIED `src/` and `tests/`. Any attempt to write there will be blocked by `tool.execute.before` hook.

5. **HEALTH MONITORING**: `gx-health-compute.sh` runs every 10 tool calls. Check `.hivemind/state/health-metrics.json` for `hard_blocked: true` which indicates critical signal failure.

## 1. HOOK INJECTION MAP

| Hook | Trigger | Reads | Injects | Side Effects |
|------|---------|-------|---------|--------------|
| **session-lifecycle.ts** | `experimental.chat.system.transform` (EVERY TURN) | `.hivemind/config.json`, `.hivemind/state/brain.json`, `hierarchy.json`, `graph/mems.json`, `graph/tasks.json` | `<hivemind>` prompt block with governance signals, bootstrap context, status blocks | Queues mutations via `queueStateMutation()` |
| **compaction.ts** | `experimental.chat.compaction.transform` (on compaction) | `brain.json`, `hierarchy.json`, `anchors.json`, `graph/tasks.json`, `graph/mems.json` | `output.context.push()` — hierarchy tree, session info, anchors, tasks | Queues mutations (clears `next_compaction_report`, sets `compaction_limit_reached`) |
| **messages-transform.ts** | Message transform (pre-stop) | `brain.json`, `graph/tasks.json`, `hierarchy.json` | Synthetic parts (PREPEND: anchors, cognitive state; APPEND: checklist) | Queues mutations for recent_messages, first_turn_confirmation, offtrack_todo_pending |
| **event-handler.ts** | Session events (session.idle, session.compacted, todo.updated, etc.) | `brain.json`, `config.json` | No prompt injection (event-driven) | Queues mutations for metrics, task manifest |
| **soft-governance.ts** | `tool.execute.after` (EVERY TOOL CALL) | `brain.json`, `config.json`, `graph/tasks.json`, `trajectory.json` | No direct prompt injection (writes counters for session-lifecycle to read) | Queues mutations for turn_count, governance_counters, violation_count, auto-commit triggers |
| **tool-gate.ts** | `tool.execute.before` (EVERY TOOL CALL) | `brain.json`, `config.json`, `graph/tasks.json`, `trajectory.json`, `hierarchy.json` | Returns advisory warnings (HC1: never blocks) | Queues mutations for files_touched, drift_score |
| **swarm-executor.ts** | SDK-backed swarm spawning | No file reads | No prompt injection | Uses OpenCode SDK to create sub-sessions via `client.session.create()` |
| **sdk-context.ts** | Plugin initialization | No file reads | SDK client context | Initializes OpenCode SDK client for other hooks |

## 3. LIBRARY CORE MAP

### 3.1 `paths.ts` — Single Source of Truth

**All `.hivemind/` paths resolve through this file:**

```
.hivemind/
├── config.json              # Project configuration
├── manifest.json            # Root manifest
├── INDEX.md                 # Documentation
├── state/
│   ├── brain.json           # Runtime session state
│   ├── hierarchy.json       # Tree structure
│   ├── anchors.json         # Persistent anchors
│   └── tasks.json           # (legacy) task manifest
├── memory/
│   └── mems.json            # Memory store
├── graph/
│   ├── trajectory.json      # Session lineage
│   ├── plans.json           # Plan nodes
│   ├── tasks.json           # Task nodes
│   ├── mems.json            # Memory nodes
│   └── orphans.json         # Quarantine
├── sessions/
│   ├── active/              # Active session files
│   └── archive/             # Archived sessions
├── codemap/                 # Codebase structure
├── logs/                    # Log files
└── templates/               # Session templates
```

**Key Functions:**
- `getEffectivePaths(projectRoot)` — Returns all paths (main entry)
- `getHierarchyPath(projectRoot)` — Resolves hierarchy.json
- `buildSessionFilename()` — Session file naming

### 3.2 `state-mutation-queue.ts` — CQRS Mutation Queue

**Purpose**: Hooks are read-only, but need to queue state updates.

**Mechanism:**
1. Hook calls `queueStateMutation({ type, payload, source })`
2. Mutation stored in module-scoped `mutationQueue[]` (max 100)
3. Tool calls `flushMutations(stateManager)` before write
4. Mutations sorted by priority, deep-merged into state
5. `stateManager.save(mergedState)` — atomic write

**Mutation Types:**
- `UPDATE_STATE` — Full state update
- `UPDATE_HIERARCHY` — Hierarchy change
- `UPDATE_METRICS` — Metrics update
- `UPDATE_SESSION` — Session metadata
- `UPDATE_FRAMEWORK_SELECTION` — Framework choice

### 3.3 `hierarchy-tree.ts` — Tree Engine

**Structure:**
```typescript
interface HierarchyTree {
  version: 1;
  root: HierarchyNode | null;  // Trajectory node
  cursor: string | null;       // Current focus
}

interface HierarchyNode {
  id: string;        // t_301411022026
  level: "trajectory" | "tactic" | "action";
  content: string;
  status: "active" | "pending" | "complete" | "blocked";
  stamp: string;     // MiMiHrHrDDMMYYYY
  children: HierarchyNode[];
}
```

**Key Functions:**
- `createNode()`, `setRoot()`, `addChild()`, `moveCursor()`
- `toBrainProjection()` — Projects tree to flat `{ trajectory, tactic, action }`
- `toAsciiTree()` — Renders for prompt injection

---

**No schema conflicts detected.** The schemas are well-structured with clear separation of concerns.

## 5. ENTRY POINT MAP

| Entry | Type | Triggers | Auto-executes? |
|-------|------|----------|----------------|
| **dist/index.js** | Module entry | Plugin import | ❌ NO — requires explicit import |
| **dist/cli.js** | CLI binary | `hivemind` command | ✅ YES — on CLI invocation |
| **npm run build** | Build script | TypeScript compilation | ❌ NO — manual trigger |
| **npm run test** | Test script | Test suite | ❌ NO — manual trigger |
| **npm run guard:public** | CI gate | Pre-push check | ❌ NO — manual/CI trigger |
| **scripts/guard-public-branch.sh** | Bash guard | Blocks sensitive files from master | ❌ NO — CI/manual |
| **scripts/validate-framework.sh** | Bash validator | Framework contract checks | ❌ NO — manual/CI |
| **scripts/check-sdk-boundary.sh** | Bash lint | SDK boundary enforcement | ❌ NO — CI/manual |

**Auto-Execution Analysis:**
- **NO automatic hooks at build time** — hooks only fire at runtime via OpenCode SDK
- **NO auto-executing scripts** — all require explicit invocation
- **Plugin loads on OpenCode session start** — hooks register with SDK

---

## 6. CROSS-CONTAMINATION ASSESSMENT

### Potential Contamination Vectors

| Vector | Risk Level | Evidence | Mitigation |
|--------|------------|----------|------------|
| **Hooks writing to `.hivemind/`** | ✅ LOW | All hooks use `queueStateMutation()` — CQRS compliant | Queue is flushed only by tools, not hooks |
| **Tools writing directly** | ⚠️ MEDIUM | Some tools bypass queue (hivemind-cycle.ts uses direct `stateManager.save()`) | Should migrate to queue pattern |
| **`.opencode/` overlap** | ⚠️ MEDIUM | `validate-framework.sh` checks parity between root and `.opencode/` | Explicit sync required |
| **SDK boundary violations** | ✅ LOW | `scripts/check-sdk-boundary.sh` enforces `lib/` is SDK-free | CI enforcement |
| **Brain.json race conditions** | ✅ LOW | `file-lock.ts` provides advisory locking | Locking on critical writes |
| **Mutation queue overflow** | ⚠️ MEDIUM | Max 100 mutations; oldest dropped FIFO | Could lose state if queue not flushed |

### Isolation Analysis

**Good Isolation:**
- ✅ Hooks are read-only (CQRS pattern)
- ✅ Tools own write operations
- ✅ `paths.ts` is single source of truth
- ✅ SDK boundary enforced by CI

**Risk Areas:**
- ⚠️ Some tools bypass mutation queue (direct `stateManager.save()`)
- ⚠️ No `.opencode/` auto-sync — could diverge from root assets
- ⚠️ `event-handler.ts` queues mutations without flush trigger (relies on next tool call)

---

## 7. CRITICAL FINDINGS

### 7.1 CQRS Compliance Status
- **Hooks**: ✅ COMPLIANT — All use `queueStateMutation()`
- **Tools**: ⚠️ PARTIAL — Most use `flushMutations()`, but `hivemind-cycle.ts` has direct save

### 7.2 State Flow Diagram
```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    OPENCODE SESSION                          │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                              │
│  ┌─────────────────┐    ┌─────────────────┐                 │
│  │ tool.execute.   │    │ tool.execute.   │                 │
│  │ BEFORE          │    │ AFTER           │                 │
│  │ (tool-gate.ts)  │    │ (soft-govern)   │                 │
│  └────────┬────────┘    └────────┬────────┘                 │
│           │ queueMut()          │ queueMut()                │
│           ▼                     ▼                           │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐            │
│  │          MUTATION QUEUE (max 100)            │            │
│  │  - UPDATE_STATE, UPDATE_METRICS, etc.       │            │
│  └─────────────────────┬───────────────────────┘            │
│                        │                                     │
│                        │ flushMutations()                    │
│                        ▼                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐            │
│  │              TOOLS LAYER                     │            │
│  │  hivemind-session, hivemind-context, etc.   │            │
│  │  (write operations)                         │            │
│  └─────────────────────┬───────────────────────┘            │
│                        │                                     │
│                        ▼                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐            │
│  │           .hivemind/state/brain.json        │            │
│  │           .hivemind/graph/*.json            │            │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────┘            │
│                                                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐            │
│  │      session-lifecycle.ts (EVERY TURN)       │            │
│  │      Reads brain.json → injects <hivemind>  │            │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────┘            │
│                                                              │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 7.3 Recommendations for hivefiver

1. **Fix CQRS Violation**: Migrate `hivemind-cycle.ts` to use `flushMutations()` pattern
2. **Add Queue Flush Event**: Consider adding explicit flush on session.idle event
3. **Monitor Queue Depth**: Add logging when queue approaches 100-item limit
4. **Document Mutation Sources**: Each `queueStateMutation()` should have unique source identifier

Excellent. All three hivexplorer agents returned comprehensive reports. Let me now synthesize the "Infection Graph" — the hierarchical outline of context-injection triggers and false-directive emitters.

Let me analyze the findings:

## TWO PARALLEL AUTO-INJECTION SYSTEMS DISCOVERED

This is a critical finding. There are **TWO separate hook/plugin systems** operating simultaneously:

### System 1: `.opencode/plugins/hiveops-governance/` (The Meta-Builder Layer)
- **context-injection.ts** — `messages.transform` hook — injects EVERY TURN
  - Reads: `.hivemind/state/todo.json`, `hierarchy.json`, `runtime-profile.json`, `health-metrics.json`, `context-recovery.json`, `enforcement.json`
  - Injects: system message with agent profile, TODOs, hierarchy cursor, health signals, constraints, scope violations, context recovery, hard block warnings, **hivefiver blindness enforcement**
  
- **delegation.ts** — `tool.execute.before/after` hooks
  - Before: blocks unauthorized operations via `gx-enforce.sh`
  - After: runs `gx-health-compute.sh` (12 signal scripts), `gx-mid-guard.sh`, `gx-auto-purge.sh` every 10 calls

- **events.ts** — session lifecycle events
  - On session.created/started: runs `gx-entry-guard.sh`, `gx-first-turn-refresh.sh`
  - On session.completed/idle: runs `gx-handoff-purify.sh`

- **compaction.ts** — compaction transform
  - Reads `context-recovery.json`
  - Injects into `output.context`

### System 2: `src/hooks/` (The Product Engine Layer)
- **session-lifecycle.ts** — `experimental.chat.system.transform` (EVERY TURN)
  - Reads: `.hivemind/config.json`, `brain.json`, `hierarchy.json`, `graph/mems.json`, `graph/tasks.json`
  - Injects: `<hivemind>` prompt block with governance signals, bootstrap context, status blocks
  - Queues mutations via `queueStateMutation()`

- **messages-transform.ts** — message transform
  - Reads: `brain.json`, `graph/tasks.json`, `hierarchy.json`
  - PREPEND: anchors, cognitive state
  - APPEND: checklist
  - Queues mutations for recent_messages, first_turn_confirmation, offtrack_todo_pending

- **compaction.ts** (src version) — compaction transform
  - Reads: `brain.json`, `hierarchy.json`, `anchors.json`, `graph/tasks.json`, `graph/mems.json`
  - Injects hierarchy tree, session info, anchors, tasks

- **soft-governance.ts** — `tool.execute.after` (EVERY TOOL CALL)
  - Reads: `brain.json`, `config.json`, `graph/tasks.json`, `trajectory.json`
  - Writes counters for session-lifecycle to read
  - Queues mutations for turn_count, governance_counters, violation_count

- **tool-gate.ts** — `tool.execute.before` (EVERY TOOL CALL)
  - Reads: `brain.json`, `config.json`, `graph/tasks.json`, `trajectory.json`, `hierarchy.json`
  - Returns advisory warnings

- **event-handler.ts** — session events
  - Queues mutations for metrics, task manifest

## THE DUAL-INJECTION PROBLEM

Both systems are firing simultaneously:
1. `.opencode/plugins/hiveops-governance/hooks/context-injection.ts` injects from `.hivemind/state/` (todo.json, hierarchy.json, etc.)
2. `src/hooks/session-lifecycle.ts` injects from `.hivemind/` (brain.json, hierarchy.json, etc.)

Both read from `.hivemind/` but read DIFFERENT files with DIFFERENT schemas. They inject into the session context at the SAME time. This is the core of the conflict.

Additionally, the script layer:
- `gx-context-engine` scripts (18+ scripts) run via the `.opencode/plugins/` hooks
- They compute health metrics, enforce scope, guard runtime entries
- These scripts WRITE to `.hivemind/state/health-metrics.json`, `runtime-profile.json`, `enforcement.json`
- Which are then READ by the same hooks and injected into context

## THE INFECTION GRAPH

Let me structure this as a hierarchical outline.

Now, the `.hivemind/state/` reports show that:
- All files are <24h old — NOT stale
- Skills ecosystem is "COMPLETE" with 14 hivefiver skills, 11 commands, 24 workflows
- No broken links

But this contradicts the user's experience of "extreme poisoning" and "false directives." The state files being fresh doesn't mean they're CORRECT — it means the auto-mechanisms are actively maintaining (and potentially propagating) incorrect state.

The key insight is: the DUAL INJECTION SYSTEMS are likely conflicting with each other. The `.opencode/plugins/` layer and the `src/hooks/` layer both inject context simultaneously, potentially with conflicting information from different state files.

## CRITICAL DISCOVERY: DUAL-INJECTION CONFLICT

The **root cause** of the Ouroboros Crisis is that **TWO SEPARATE auto-injection systems** fire simultaneously on every LLM turn, reading from **different state files** with **different schemas**, and injecting **overlapping but conflicting context** into the same session window.

```
                    ┌──────────────────────────────────────────┐
                    │          OPENCODE LLM SESSION             │
                    │        (shared context window)            │
                    ├──────────────┬───────────────────────────┤
                    │              │                            │
           ┌───────▼───────┐  ┌──▼──────────────────┐         │
           │  SYSTEM 1      │  │  SYSTEM 2            │        │
           │  .opencode/    │  │  src/hooks/           │        │
           │  plugins/      │  │  (product engine)     │        │
           │  hiveops-gov/  │  │                       │        │
           │  hooks/        │  │                       │        │
           ├───────────────┤  ├───────────────────────┤        │
           │ READS:         │  │ READS:                │        │
           │ • todo.json    │  │ • brain.json          │        │
           │ • hierarchy.json│ │ • hierarchy.json  ◀── OVERLAP │
           │ • runtime-     │  │ • config.json         │        │
           │   profile.json │  │ • graph/mems.json     │        │
           │ • health-      │  │ • graph/tasks.json    │        │
           │   metrics.json │  │ • trajectory.json     │        │
           │ • enforcement  │  │ • anchors.json        │        │
           │   .json        │  │                       │        │
           │ • context-     │  │                       │        │
           │   recovery.json│  │                       │        │
           └───────┬───────┘  └──────────┬────────────┘        │
                   │                      │                     │
                   ▼                      ▼                     │
           ┌──────────────────────────────────────────┐        │
           │      CONFLICTING CONTEXT INJECTION        │        │
           │  System 1: agent profile + TODOs +        │        │
           │    hierarchy cursor + health signals +    │        │
           │    blindness enforcement                  │        │
           │  System 2: <hivemind> block + anchors +   │        │
           │    cognitive state + checklist + tasks     │        │
           └──────────────────────────────────────────┘        │
                    └──────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

## INFECTION ZONE 1: `.opencode/plugins/hiveops-governance/` — The Meta Layer

### Auto-Firing Hooks (EVERY TURN, NO OPT-OUT)

| Hook File | Trigger | Frequency | Infection Vector |
|-----------|---------|-----------|------------------|
| `hooks/context-injection.ts` (351L) | `messages.transform` | **EVERY TURN** | 🔴 Prepends system message reading 6 state files |
| `hooks/delegation.ts` (217L) | `tool.execute.before/after` | **EVERY TOOL CALL** | 🔴 Before: blocks ops via `gx-enforce.sh`. After: runs `gx-health-compute.sh` every 10 calls |
| `hooks/events.ts` (109L) | session lifecycle events | **ON SESSION START/END** | 🟡 Runs `gx-entry-guard.sh`, `gx-first-turn-refresh.sh` |
| `hooks/compaction.ts` (208L) | `session.compacting` | **ON COMPACTION** | 🟡 Injects recovery context from `context-recovery.json` |

### Downstream Scripts Triggered By Hooks

```
hooks/context-injection.ts (EVERY TURN)
    └── reads 6 state files → injects system message

hooks/delegation.ts (EVERY TOOL CALL)
    ├── BEFORE: gx-enforce.sh (565L) ← scope/delegation enforcement
    └── AFTER (every 10 calls):
        ├── gx-health-compute.sh (389L) ← runs 12 signal scripts
        │   └── signals/gx-signal-*.sh × 12
        ├── gx-mid-guard.sh ← mid-session guard
        └── gx-auto-purge.sh ← auto-purge stale data

hooks/events.ts (ON SESSION START)
    ├── gx-entry-guard.sh (235L) ← builds runtime-profile.json
    ├── gx-first-turn-refresh.sh ← refreshes all state
    └── gx-handoff-purify.sh ← purifies handoffs

hooks/compaction.ts (ON COMPACTION)
    └── gx-context-retrieve.sh ← synthesizes recovery context
```

---

## INFECTION ZONE 2: `src/hooks/` — The Product Engine Layer

### Auto-Firing Hooks (EVERY TURN, NO OPT-OUT)

| Hook File | Trigger | Frequency | Infection Vector |
|-----------|---------|-----------|------------------|
| `session-lifecycle.ts` | `system.transform` | **EVERY TURN** | 🔴 Injects `<hivemind>` block + queues mutations |
| `messages-transform.ts` | message transform | **EVERY TURN** | 🔴 PREPEND anchors/cognitive state, APPEND checklist |
| `soft-governance.ts` | `tool.execute.after` | **EVERY TOOL CALL** | 🟡 Writes counters → read by session-lifecycle next turn |
| `tool-gate.ts` | `tool.execute.before` | **EVERY TOOL CALL** | 🟢 Advisory only (never blocks) |
| `compaction.ts` (src) | compaction transform | **ON COMPACTION** | 🟡 Injects hierarchy tree + session info |
| `event-handler.ts` | lifecycle events | **ON EVENTS** | 🟢 Queues mutations only |

### State Mutation Flow

```
src/hooks/ (read-only, CQRS-compliant)
    ├── queue mutations via queueStateMutation()
    │   └── stored in module-scoped mutationQueue[] (max 100)
    │
src/tools/ (write operations)
    ├── flushMutations(stateManager) ← drains queue, merges state
    │   └── deep-merge → stateManager.save() → .hivemind/state/brain.json
    │
    └── EXCEPTION: hivemind-cycle.ts bypasses queue (direct save) ⚠️
```

---

## INFECTION ZONE 3: `.hivemind/state/` — The Contested Ground

These state files are **READ BY BOTH SYSTEMS** simultaneously:

| State File | Read by System 1 | Read by System 2 | Written by | Conflict Risk |
|------------|-------------------|-------------------|------------|---------------|
| `hierarchy.json` | ✅ context-injection.ts | ✅ session-lifecycle.ts | src/tools/, gx-todo-sync.sh | 🔴 **HIGH** — both systems read + interpret differently |
| `todo.json` | ✅ context-injection.ts | ❌ | hiveops_todo tool, gx-todo-sync.sh | 🟡 Single reader |
| `brain.json` | ❌ | ✅ session-lifecycle.ts + 5 hooks | src/tools/hivemind-session.ts | 🟡 Single reader |
| `runtime-profile.json` | ✅ context-injection.ts | ❌ | gx-entry-guard.sh | 🟡 Single reader |
| `health-metrics.json` | ✅ context-injection.ts | ❌ | gx-health-compute.sh | 🟡 Single reader |
| `enforcement.json` | ✅ delegation.ts + events.ts | ❌ | gx-enforce.sh | 🟡 Single reader |
| `context-recovery.json` | ✅ compaction.ts (plugin) | ❌ | gx-context-retrieve.sh | 🟡 Single reader |

**The `hierarchy.json` is the single most dangerous shared file** — both systems read it, format it differently, and inject it into the same context window creating contradictory hierarchy views.

## THE INFECTION CASCADE (How False Directives Propagate)

```
SESSION START
    │
    ├─→ gx-entry-guard.sh → writes runtime-profile.json
    ├─→ gx-first-turn-refresh.sh → refreshes all state
    │
    ▼
EVERY LLM TURN (dual injection)
    │
    ├─→ System 1: context-injection.ts reads 6 files → injects system msg
    ├─→ System 2: session-lifecycle.ts reads 5 files → injects <hivemind>
    ├─→ System 2: messages-transform.ts → PREPEND anchors + APPEND checklist
    │
    ▼
EVERY TOOL CALL
    │
    ├─→ System 1: delegation.ts BEFORE → gx-enforce.sh (scope check)
    ├─→ System 2: tool-gate.ts BEFORE → advisory warnings
    ├─→ System 2: soft-governance.ts AFTER → update counters
    ├─→ System 1: delegation.ts AFTER (every 10th) → gx-health-compute.sh
    │       └─→ 12 signal scripts → writes health-metrics.json
    │              └─→ NEXT TURN: context-injection.ts reads it → injects
    │
    ▼
IF STATE FILES BECOME STALE/CONFLICTING:
    │
    ├─→ context-injection.ts injects wrong TODOs/hierarchy/health
    ├─→ session-lifecycle.ts injects contradictory <hivemind> block
    ├─→ Agent role-drifts based on false injected constraints
    ├─→ Delegations blocked/misdirected by stale enforcement.json
    ├─→ Health signals show phantom degradation → trigger false L3/L4 alerts
    │
    ▼
COMPACTION (context reset attempt)
    │
    ├─→ System 1: compaction.ts → injects context-recovery.json (possibly stale)
    ├─→ System 2: compaction.ts (src) → injects hierarchy tree (possibly different)
    └─→ Post-compact session inherits BOTH stale recovery contexts
```

## TOP-3 FALSE EMITTERS (Ranked by Damage Potential)

| Rank | Emitter | Location | Why It's Dangerous |
|------|---------|----------|--------------------|
| **#1** | `context-injection.ts` | `.opencode/plugins/hiveops-governance/hooks/` | **Fires EVERY turn. Reads 6 state files. If ANY is stale → entire session context is polluted. Includes special "blindness enforcement" for hivefiver that prevents self-investigation.** |
| **#2** | `session-lifecycle.ts` | `src/hooks/` | **Fires EVERY turn. Reads DIFFERENT 5 state files. Injects `<hivemind>` block that CONFLICTS with System 1's injection. Both inject hierarchy data but format it differently.** |
| **#3** | `gx-health-compute.sh` + 12 signal scripts | `.opencode/skills/gx-context-engine/scripts/` | **Runs every 10 tool calls. Computes 12 "health signals" that become "facts" injected next turn. If signal scripts produce garbage → garbage becomes "truth" in context.** |

By forcing the agents into a read-only investigation swarm, you bypassed the immediate hallucination loop and extracted the actual mechanical truth of your system.

Furthermore, **your human intuition caught the exact real-world edge cases the AI missed.** LLMs naturally assume a single, linear, continuous execution thread, blinding them to the realities of human-in-the-loop development (taking weekends off, running multiple terminal tabs).

Here is the evaluation of the two approaches, an analysis of the critical gaps, and the consolidated **Phase 3 Master Directive** to pass to the winning instance.

---

### 1. The Verdict: Radical vs. Accurate

**Team A is the most RADICAL (and strategically correct).**

* **The Win:** They zoomed out and diagnosed the "Ouroboros" root cause: the **Dual-Injection Conflict**. They realized that the product engine (`src/hooks/`) and the meta-framework plugin (`.opencode/plugins/hiveops-governance/`) are engaged in a turf war. They are firing simultaneously, reading the same contested `.json` state files (like `hierarchy.json`), and vomiting overlapping, conflicting context into the LLM's system prompt on *every single turn*.
* **The Gap:** They panicked at the fire and skipped the strict mapping instructions requested in Phase 2.

**Team B is the most ACCURATE (and structurally essential).**

* **The Win:** They executed a flawless topological map of the Directed Acyclic Graph (DAG). Their "Skeleton Matrix" perfectly mapped the **L0–L3 Progressive Disclosure** paths and the exact script lineage. We *need* this exact map in the agent's context window to safely refactor the system without breaking the chain.
* **The Gap:** They noticed the file overlaps but treated them as a static structural footnote rather than a critical runtime emergency. A perfect map of a burning building doesn't put out the fire.

### 2. The Blind Spots: Your Nuances Validated

Both swarms missed two massive architectural flaws that will destroy the framework in production. We must add these to the "False Emitters" list immediately:

**GAP 1: The Wall-Clock Staleness Fallacy (The Time-Bomb)**

* **The Bug:** Scripts like `gx-signal-hierarchy-freshness.sh` and `staleness.ts` use hardcoded Unix epoch timestamps (e.g., `STALE_THRESHOLD_SECONDS=86400`, or a decay rate per minute) to calculate context rot.
* **The Reality:** A developer pauses work on Friday and resumes Monday. The system hallucinates a "CRITICAL DRIFT!" and triggers a catastrophic auto-purge or forces a pivot—even though zero code changed.
* **The Fix:** Staleness must be **Relational/Topological**, not chronological. A planning artifact is only "stale" if the underlying codebase (`git diff`) has mutated outside the session's awareness, or if the uncompleted `tactic/action` row-chains diverge. Time passing is irrelevant.

**GAP 2: Singleton State Bottlenecks (The Multi-Session Crossfire)**

* **The Bug:** Both teams accept `.hivemind/state/todo.json`, `hierarchy.json`, and `STATE.md` as global singletons.
* **The Reality:** OpenCode allows users to run multiple sessions simultaneously (e.g., Session A building a UI component, Session B debugging a backend route). Because both sessions read/write to the exact same global `todo.json` and `STATE.md`, Session A's background hook will overwrite the cursor and poison the context window of Session B on its next turn.
* **The Fix:** State files must be explicitly partitioned by `session_id` or `trajectory_id` (e.g., `.hivemind/sessions/<id>/todo.json`). The context-injector must strictly bind its reads to the *active* session's lineage.

---

We must merge **Team A's Radical Decoupling** with **Team B's Golden Path Skeleton**, while injecting **Your Multi-Session/Relational Axioms**.

We cannot safely rewrite `hivefiver-prime` (the markdown instructions) until we stop the system from actively lying to the LLM. Therefore, **Node 1 MUST be the Hook Injection & State Concurrency Layer.**

Pass this feedback and exact prompt back to the **Team B Swarm** (since they hold the correct structural map in their context memory), but we will forcefully inject Team A's dual-injection findings and your human nuances into their directive.

  ├── gx-auto-purge.sh → dirty score > 90 auto-purge
  └── + 4 more (sot-register, decision-log, workflow-state, scope-resolve)

hivefiver-mode/scripts/
  ├── route-stage.sh → reads hierarchy.json
  ├── classify-intent.sh → produces intent JSON
  └── guided-discovery.sh → produces user profile JSON

hivefiver-coordination/scripts/
  ├── runtime-gate.sh → pre-turn, checkpoint, post-turn gates
  ├── quality-check.sh, gate-check.sh, state-update.sh
  └── pipeline-orchestrator.sh, hivefiver-must-pack.sh
```

## 6. ENTRY VARIANT ROUTING

### Variant 1: New Session
```
events.ts → gx-entry-guard.sh → gx-first-turn-refresh.sh
hivefiver.md → hivefiver-prime → hivefiver-mode
  └── route-stage.sh → reads hierarchy.json, STATE.md
  └── classify-intent.sh → produces intent JSON
```

### Variant 2: Post-Compaction Recovery
```
compaction.ts → gx-handoff-purify.sh → gx-schema-sync.sh → gx-context-retrieve.sh
context-injection.ts → reads context-recovery.json → injects trajectory_summary
hivefiver-prime §2 → Compact Continuity Protocol → resumes from "next action"
```

### Variant 3: Delegated Sub-Session
```
delegation.ts → gx-enforce.sh check-delegation → gx-trace-check.sh
hivefiver.md (sub-session mode) → NO user confirmation → return structured evidence
```

## 7. CONFLICT SURFACES (10 Identified)

| # | Paths | Conflict |
|---|-------|----------|
| 1 | `hivefiver-prime` ↔ `hivemind-governance` | Both claim "load first" — different agents, shared entry |
| 2 | `hivefiver.md` ↔ `hivefiver-start.md` | Root router vs specific stage — keyword match resolution |
| 3 | `gx-health-compute.sh` ↔ `health-metrics.json` | Script writes, plugin reads — race condition risk |
| 4 | `route-stage.sh` ↔ `hierarchy.json` | Concurrent mutations cause stale reads |
| 5 | `context-injection.ts` ↔ 5 state files | Reads 5 files every turn — any stale file = poisoned context |
| 6 | `runtime-gate.sh` ↔ `gx-mid-guard.sh` | Both fire mid-session — duplicate enforcement overhead |
| 7 | **hivefiver.md blindness** ↔ **context-injection.ts blindness enforcement** | **DOUBLE ENFORCEMENT** |
| 8 | `hivefiver-vibecoder.yaml` ↔ `enterprise-architect.yaml` | Same stages, different skill_bundles — routing collision |
| 9 | `STATE.md` ↔ `hierarchy.json` | **DUAL SOURCE OF TRUTH** — pipeline vs trajectory |
| 10 | `context-integrity` ↔ `context-quality-escalation` | Escalation deprecated but file still exists |

---

## 8. MINIMUM GOLDEN PATH (Verified Clean Turn)

```
User: /hivefiver start "build me a skill"

1. events.ts → gx-entry-guard.sh [builds profile]
             → gx-first-turn-refresh.sh [refreshes stale]

2. hivefiver.md → hivefiver-prime → hivefiver-mode

3. hivefiver-start.md → gate-check.sh [G0 entry]
                       → classify-intent.sh [→ intent: build_new]
                       → guided-discovery.sh [→ user profile]
                       → runtime-gate.sh pre-turn [MANDATORY]

4. hivefiver-mode → reads hierarchy.json, STATE.md
                   → determines stage: start, next_command: /hivefiver discovery

5. hivefiver-coordination → enforces G0: scope valid, context present

6. hivefiver-start.md → state-update.sh [writes STATE.md]
                       → runtime-gate.sh post-turn [MANDATORY]
                       → produces output_contract

7. context-injection.ts → injects updated TODO, hierarchy cursor, health signals

8. Gate 0 CLOSES → Output includes must_pack + runtime_gate_post_turn evidence
```

## 9. KEY FINDINGS FOR PHASE 3 SYNTHESIS

### Critical Issues
1. **Dual-Blindness Enforcement**: Agent frontmatter declares `read:deny` BUT plugin also enforces blindness injection at `context-injection.ts:294-330` — redundant overhead
2. **Dual Source of Truth**: `STATE.md` (pipeline) vs `hierarchy.json` (trajectory) — risk of divergence
3. **Race Conditions**: `gx-health-compute.sh` writes `health-metrics.json` while plugin reads it same turn
4. **Duplicate Mid-Session Enforcement**: `runtime-gate.sh` + `gx-mid-guard.sh` both fire every 10 tool calls

- `gx-semantic-validate.sh` — stub until R4
- `gx-sot-register.sh` — marked stub

### 1.3 HIVEFIVER BLINDNESS ENFORCEMENT (Lines 294-330)

**EXACT CODE:**

```typescript
// Lines 294-330
// === HIVEFIVER-SPECIFIC BLINDNESS ENFORCEMENT ===
// hivefiver has read:deny, glob:deny, grep:deny — intentionally blind.
// This block injects mandatory delegation awareness EVERY turn.
if (state.current.agent === "hivefiver") {
  const delegatedToExplorer = state.current.delegationChain.some(
    (entry) => entry.to === "hivexplorer"
  )
  const turnCount = state.current.turnCount

  // Determine entry type
  let entryType: "first_entry" | "mid_session" | "post_compact" = "mid_session"
  if (turnCount <= 1) entryType = "first_entry"
  if (recovery) entryType = "post_compact"

  // Severity escalation based on turns without hivexplorer delegation
  let severity = "SEV-1 MONITOR"
  if (turnCount >= 12 && !delegatedToExplorer) severity = "SEV-3 CRITICAL"
  else if (turnCount >= 8 && !delegatedToExplorer) severity = "SEV-2 ELEVATED"
  else if (turnCount >= 4 && !delegatedToExplorer) severity = "SEV-1 WARNING"

  contextLines.push("")
  contextLines.push("### HIVEFIVER BLINDNESS ENFORCEMENT [ALWAYS-ON]")
  contextLines.push(`**Entry:** ${entryType} | **Severity:** ${severity}`)
  contextLines.push(
    `**Delegated to hivexplorer:** ${delegatedToExplorer ? "YES" : "NO — REQUIRED BEFORE ANY ACTION"}`
  )
  contextLines.push("")
  contextLines.push("YOU ARE BLIND. You have read:deny, glob:deny, grep:deny, bash:deny.")
  contextLines.push("GOLDEN RULE: Before creating, modifying, or claiming anything about existing files,")
  contextLines.push("you MUST delegate to hivexplorer for verification. No exceptions.")

  if (!delegatedToExplorer && turnCount >= 4) {
    contextLines.push("")
    contextLines.push(`**${severity}: ${turnCount} turns without hivexplorer verification.**`)
    contextLines.push("HIGH RISK of hallucination. Delegate to hivexplorer NOW or STOP.")
  }
}
```

### 2.2 EXACT FORMAT OF `<hivemind>` BLOCK

```typescript
// Lines 219-230
function assembleSections(sections: string[][], budget: number, log: Logger): string {
  const finalLines: string[] = ["<hivemind>"]
  for (const section of sections) {
    if (section.length === 0) continue
    const deduped = dedupeContextLines(section).lines
    if (deduped.length === 0) continue
    const candidate = [...finalLines, ...deduped, "</hivemind>"].join("\n")
    if (candidate.length <= budget) finalLines.push(...deduped)
    else log.debug(`Section dropped due to budget: ${section[0]?.slice(0, 40)}...`)
  }
  finalLines.push("</hivemind>")
  return finalLines.join("\n")
}
```

| **Reads config.json?** | **YES** — Line 98: `const config = await loadConfig(directory)` |
| **Session-scoped?** | **PARTIAL** — Uses `input.sessionID` for early exit but paths are project-global |

function buildAnchorContext(state: BrainState): string {
  const phase = state.hierarchy.trajectory || "Unset"
  const task = state.hierarchy.action || "Unset"
  const hierarchyStatus = state.metrics.context_updates > 0 ? "Active" : "Stale"

  return `[SYSTEM ANCHOR: ${phase} | Active Task: ${task} | Hierarchy: ${hierarchyStatus}]`
}

    message.parts = [syntheticPart, ...message.parts]
    return
  }
  // ... legacy message handling
}

## FILE 5: `.opencode/skills/gx-context-engine/scripts/signals/gx-signal-hierarchy-freshness.sh`

### 5.1 EXACT STALENESS CALCULATION LOGIC

```bash
# Lines 78-87 — Unix epoch comparison
mtime_epoch=$(get_mtime_epoch "$HIERARCHY_FILE")
now_epoch=$(date +%s)
if [ "$mtime_epoch" -le 0 ]; then
  age_seconds=0
else
  age_seconds=$((now_epoch - mtime_epoch))
  if [ "$age_seconds" -lt 0 ]; then
    age_seconds=0
  fi
fi
```

### 5.2 STALE_THRESHOLD_SECONDS

**NO FIXED THRESHOLD.** Uses **decay_rate per minute**:

```bash
# Lines 36-52 — Decay rate configuration
decay_rate=10  # Default: 10 points per minute
if [ "$AGENT_LEVEL" = "3" ]; then
  decay_rate=5  # Level 3 agents decay slower
fi

# Can be overridden from enforcement.json
if [ -f "$ENFORCEMENT_FILE" ]; then
  configured_decay=$(jq -r --arg level "$AGENT_LEVEL" '
    if .hierarchyFreshnessDecayRates then
      (.hierarchyFreshnessDecayRates[$level] // empty)
    else
      empty
    end
  ' "$ENFORCEMENT_FILE" 2>/dev/null || echo "")
  if [[ "$configured_decay" =~ ^[0-9]+$ ]]; then
    decay_rate="$configured_decay"
  fi
fi
```

### 5.3 FRESHNESS SCORING FORMULA

```bash
# Lines 89-97 — Score calculation
age_minutes=$((age_seconds / 60))
score=$((100 - (age_minutes * decay_rate)))

if [ "$score" -lt 0 ]; then
  score=0
fi
if [ "$score" -gt 100 ]; then
  score=100
fi
```

**Formula**: `score = clamp(100 - (age_minutes * decay_rate), 0, 100)`

**Effective stale threshold**:
- Default decay_rate=10 → Score reaches 0 at **10 minutes**
- Level 3 decay_rate=5 → Score reaches 0 at **20 minutes**

---

// Lines 41-123 — Complete HivemindPaths interface
export interface HivemindPaths {
  root: string              // .hivemind/
  config: string            // .hivemind/config.json
  index: string             // .hivemind/INDEX.md
  rootManifest: string      // .hivemind/manifest.json

  // state/ (hot — updated every turn)
  stateDir: string
  stateManifest: string
  brain: string             // state/brain.json
  hierarchy: string         // state/hierarchy.json

### 6.2 SESSION-SCOPING ANALYSIS

| Feature | Value |
|---------|-------|
| **Session-scoped paths?** | **NO** — All paths are **project-global** |
| **session_id partitioning?** | **NO** — No session_id in any path definition |
| **Active session resolution** | **DYNAMIC** — Reads `sessions/manifest.json` to find active session file |

```typescript
// Lines 458-488 — Active session path is resolved dynamically, not built-in
export async function getActiveSessionPath(
  projectRoot: string,
): Promise<string | null> {
  const paths = getHivemindPaths(projectRoot)

  if (!existsSync(paths.sessionsManifest)) {
    return null
  }

  try {
    const raw = await readFile(paths.sessionsManifest, "utf-8")
    const manifest = JSON.parse(raw) as SessionManifest

    if (!manifest.active_stamp) {
      return null
    }

    const entry = manifest.sessions.find(
      (s) => s.stamp === manifest.active_stamp,
    )
    if (!entry) {
      return null
    }

    // Active sessions live in sessions/active/ in the new structure
    return safeJoinWithin(paths.activeDir, entry.file)
  } catch {
    return null
  }
}
```

## FIX 1: DUAL-INJECTION DECOUPLING

### The Problem (Verified)

Two independent injection systems fire on **every LLM turn**, unaware of each other:

| System | File | Channel | Agent-Aware? | Session-Scoped? |
|--------|------|---------|-------------|-----------------|
| **System 1** (Meta/Plugin) | `context-injection.ts` | `output.messages[]` (prepend msg) | PARTIAL (hivefiver block) | NO |
| **System 2a** (Product/Engine) | `session-lifecycle.ts` | `output.system[]` (system prompt) | NO | PARTIAL (sessionID gate) |
| **System 2b** (Product/Engine) | `messages-transform.ts` | `output.messages[].parts[]` (synthetic parts) | NO | PARTIAL (Set gate) |

Both read `hierarchy.json`. Both inject hierarchy data. Different formats. **The LLM sees contradictory hierarchy views.**

### The Decoupling Strategy: Agent-Domain Routing

**Principle**: System 1 owns `hivefiver` sessions. System 2 owns all other agent sessions. Neither fires for the other's domain.

#### 1A. Modify `context-injection.ts` — Add Agent Guard

**Current code** (line 179-181):
```typescript
return async (input: any, output: any) => {
  if (!output.messages || !Array.isArray(output.messages)) return
  // PROCEEDS UNCONDITIONALLY
```

**Proposed code**:
```typescript
return async (input: any, output: any) => {
  if (!output.messages || !Array.isArray(output.messages)) return
  
  // DECOUPLING GUARD: System 1 (GX-Pack) ONLY fires for meta-builder agents
  const META_BUILDER_AGENTS = ["hivefiver"] as const
  const currentAgent = state.current.agent
  if (!META_BUILDER_AGENTS.includes(currentAgent as any)) {
    return // MUTED — System 2 (product engine) owns this session
  }
  
  // ... existing injection logic continues for hivefiver only
```

**Rationale**: `context-injection.ts` was built for `hivefiver`'s blindness enforcement and GX-Pack governance. It should NOT inject its governance context into `hivemaker`, `hivehealer`, or `hiveminder` sessions — those are governed by System 2.

#### 1B. Modify `session-lifecycle.ts` — Add Inverse Agent Guard

**Current code** (line 80-88):
```typescript
return async (input: { sessionID?: string; model?: unknown }, output: { system: string[] }): Promise<void> => {
  try {
    const checklist = await injectGovernanceInstruction(output, effectiveDir, input.sessionID || "unknown")
    if (!input.sessionID) {
      appendChecklistFailureReminder(output, checklist)
      return
    }
```

**Proposed code**:
```typescript
return async (input: { sessionID?: string; model?: unknown }, output: { system: string[] }): Promise<void> => {
  try {
    // DECOUPLING GUARD: System 2 (product engine) MUTES for meta-builder agents
    // Meta-builder agents are governed by System 1 (GX-Pack plugin)
    const META_BUILDER_AGENTS = ["hivefiver"]
    const agentName = resolveCurrentAgent(input) // NEW: resolve from session context
    if (META_BUILDER_AGENTS.includes(agentName)) {
      return // MUTED — System 1 (GX-Pack) owns this session
    }
    
    const checklist = await injectGovernanceInstruction(output, effectiveDir, input.sessionID || "unknown")
```

**Challenge**: `session-lifecycle.ts` currently receives `input: { sessionID?, model? }` — it does NOT receive the agent name. We need to resolve this.

**Resolution Options**:

| Option | Mechanism | Complexity |
|--------|-----------|-----------|
| **A (Recommended)** | Read agent from `brain.json` → `state.session.agent` | Low — file already read downstream |
| **B** | Pass agent via SDK hook input enhancement | Medium — requires SDK change |
| **C** | Read from OpenCode session API | High — new dependency |

**Recommended: Option A** — Load `brain.json` early in the hook to resolve the current agent:
```typescript
// NEW: resolve agent from brain state (already loaded downstream)
function resolveCurrentAgent(input: { sessionID?: string }, directory: string): string {
  try {
    const brainPath = join(directory, ".hivemind", "state", "brain.json")
    if (!existsSync(brainPath)) return "unknown"
    const brain = JSON.parse(readFileSync(brainPath, "utf-8"))
    return brain.session?.agent || "unknown"
  } catch {
    return "unknown"
  }
}
```

#### 1C. Modify `messages-transform.ts` — Same Pattern

**Current code** (line 321-324):
```typescript
const config = await loadConfig(directory)
if (config.governance_mode === "permissive") return
```

**Proposed addition** (after line 324):
```typescript
const config = await loadConfig(directory)
if (config.governance_mode === "permissive") return

// DECOUPLING GUARD: System 2 mutes for meta-builder agents
const brainState = await stateManager.load()
const currentAgent = brainState?.session?.agent || "unknown"
const META_BUILDER_AGENTS = ["hivefiver"]
if (META_BUILDER_AGENTS.includes(currentAgent)) {
  return // MUTED — System 1 (GX-Pack) governs meta-builder sessions
}
```

#### 1D. Resolve Conflict Surface #7: Double Blindness Enforcement

**Finding** (Team B): hivefiver's agent frontmatter declares `read:deny, glob:deny` AND `context-injection.ts:294-330` injects blindness enforcement text every turn.

**Decision**: Keep the plugin injection (it escalates severity based on turn count). Remove redundant text from agent frontmatter body — let the deterministic plugin be the single source.

#### 1E. Resolve Conflict Surface #9: Dual SOT (STATE.md vs hierarchy.json)

**Finding** (Team B): `STATE.md` tracks pipeline progress. `hierarchy.json` tracks trajectory tree. Both claim to be "the current state."

**Decision**: 
- `hierarchy.json` is the **runtime SOT** (read by hooks, drives cursor)
- `STATE.md` is the **human-readable log** (never read by hooks, never drives decisions)
- Add a header to `STATE.md`: `<!-- AUDIT LOG ONLY — Runtime SOT is hierarchy.json -->`

---

## FIX 2: RELATIONAL STALENESS (Kill Wall-Clock)

### The Problem (Verified)

`gx-signal-hierarchy-freshness.sh` lines 89-97:
```bash
age_minutes=$((age_seconds / 60))
score=$((100 - (age_minutes * decay_rate)))
```

With default `decay_rate=10`, the score hits **ZERO after 10 minutes**. A coffee break = "CRITICAL DRIFT."

### The Fix: Sequential/Topological Freshness

**Replace time-based decay with three relational signals:**

```bash
#!/usr/bin/env bash
# gx-signal-hierarchy-freshness.sh (REFACTORED)
# Staleness = relational drift, NOT wall-clock age

set -euo pipefail

WORKTREE="${1:-.}"
HIERARCHY_FILE="$WORKTREE/.hivemind/state/hierarchy.json"
BRAIN_FILE="$WORKTREE/.hivemind/state/brain.json"

score=100  # Start fresh, deduct for drift signals

# ─── SIGNAL 1: Git Drift (0-40 points) ───
# Has the codebase changed since the hierarchy was last updated?
# If code changed but hierarchy didn't update → stale
hierarchy_mtime=$(stat -f %m "$HIERARCHY_FILE" 2>/dev/null || echo 0)
git_last_commit=$(git -C "$WORKTREE" log -1 --format=%ct 2>/dev/null || echo 0)

if [ "$git_last_commit" -gt "$hierarchy_mtime" ]; then
  # Code changed after hierarchy last updated
  changed_files=$(git -C "$WORKTREE" diff --name-only --diff-filter=ACMR \
    --since="@$hierarchy_mtime" HEAD 2>/dev/null | wc -l | tr -d ' ')
  
  if [ "$changed_files" -gt 20 ]; then
    score=$((score - 40))  # Major drift
  elif [ "$changed_files" -gt 5 ]; then
    score=$((score - 20))  # Moderate drift  
  elif [ "$changed_files" -gt 0 ]; then
    score=$((score - 10))  # Minor drift
  fi
  # else: no changes since hierarchy update → no drift → no deduction
fi

# ─── SIGNAL 2: Row-Chain Continuity (0-35 points) ───
# Are there uncompleted tactic/action nodes that lost their parent?
orphan_count=$(jq -r '
  [.. | objects | select(.level != null and .status == "active") |
   select(.children == null or (.children | length) == 0)]
  | length
' "$HIERARCHY_FILE" 2>/dev/null || echo 0)

incomplete_chains=$(jq -r '
  [.. | objects | select(.level == "action" and .status == "pending") |
   select(.content == null or .content == "")]
  | length
' "$HIERARCHY_FILE" 2>/dev/null || echo 0)

if [ "$orphan_count" -gt 3 ] || [ "$incomplete_chains" -gt 5 ]; then
  score=$((score - 35))
elif [ "$orphan_count" -gt 0 ] || [ "$incomplete_chains" -gt 0 ]; then
  score=$((score - 15))
fi

# ─── SIGNAL 3: Session Continuity (0-25 points) ───
# Does the current session match the hierarchy's active trajectory?
session_id=$(jq -r '.session.id // empty' "$BRAIN_FILE" 2>/dev/null || echo "")
hierarchy_cursor=$(jq -r '.cursor // empty' "$HIERARCHY_FILE" 2>/dev/null || echo "")

if [ -z "$session_id" ] || [ -z "$hierarchy_cursor" ]; then
  score=$((score - 25))  # No active session or no cursor → disconnected
fi

# ─── CLAMP & OUTPUT ───
if [ "$score" -lt 0 ]; then score=0; fi
if [ "$score" -gt 100 ]; then score=100; fi

echo "$score"
```

**Key change**: A developer sleeping for 8 hours scores **100** if no code changed and the hierarchy is internally consistent. A developer making 30 code commits while the hierarchy hasn't updated scores **25** even if it was updated 2 minutes ago.

---

## FIX 3: SESSION-SCOPED STATE (Multi-Concurrency)

### The Problem (Verified)

`paths.ts` defines **ALL** state paths as project-global:
```
.hivemind/state/brain.json      ← ONE global file
.hivemind/state/hierarchy.json  ← ONE global file
.hivemind/state/todo.json       ← ONE global file
```

Two concurrent sessions read/write the same files → cross-contamination.

### The Architecture: Layered State Isolation

**Principle**: Split state into **Project-Level** (shared, rare writes) and **Session-Level** (isolated, frequent writes).

```
.hivemind/
├── config.json                          # Project-level (shared, stable)
├── state/
│   ├── hierarchy.json                   # Project-level SOT (the tree itself)
│   └── sot-index.json                   # Project-level artifact registry
│
├── sessions/
│   ├── manifest.json                    # Session registry
│   ├── active/
│   │   ├── session-<id-1>/              # Session A's isolated state
│   │   │   ├── brain.json               # Session-scoped runtime state
│   │   │   ├── todo.json                # Session-scoped TODOs
│   │   │   ├── health-metrics.json      # Session-scoped health
│   │   │   ├── runtime-profile.json     # Session-scoped profile
│   │   │   ├── enforcement.json         # Session-scoped enforcement
│   │   │   ├── context-recovery.json    # Session-scoped recovery
│   │   │   └── cursor.json              # Session's pointer into hierarchy.json
│   │   │
│   │   └── session-<id-2>/              # Session B's isolated state
│   │       ├── brain.json
│   │       ├── todo.json
│   │       └── ...
│   │
│   └── archive/                         # Completed sessions
```

### The Cursor Pattern

Instead of each session mutating the global `hierarchy.json` cursor, each session gets a **cursor.json** that points into the shared hierarchy:

```json
// sessions/active/session-abc123/cursor.json
{
  "session_id": "abc123",
  "agent": "hivefiver",
  "trajectory_id": "t_301411022026",
  "focused_node_id": "a_140511022026",
  "focused_level": "action",
  "created_at": "2026-03-03T10:00:00Z",
  "last_advanced_at": "2026-03-03T10:45:00Z"
}
```

The global `hierarchy.json` retains the tree structure and node statuses. But **which node a session is focused on** is session-local.

### Migration Path in `paths.ts`

```typescript
// NEW: Session-scoped path resolution
export function getSessionPaths(
  projectRoot: string,
  sessionId: string
): SessionScopedPaths {
  const base = getHivemindPaths(projectRoot)
  const sessionDir = join(base.activeDir, `session-${sessionId}`)
  
  return {
    // Session-isolated (hot state)
    brain: join(sessionDir, "brain.json"),
    todo: join(sessionDir, "todo.json"),
    healthMetrics: join(sessionDir, "health-metrics.json"),
    runtimeProfile: join(sessionDir, "runtime-profile.json"),
    enforcement: join(sessionDir, "enforcement.json"),
    contextRecovery: join(sessionDir, "context-recovery.json"),
    cursor: join(sessionDir, "cursor.json"),
    
    // Project-global (shared, stable)
    hierarchy: base.hierarchy,     // shared tree
    config: base.config,           // shared config
    sotIndex: base.sotIndex,       // shared artifact registry
  }
}
```

### Hook Consumer Changes

Every hook that reads state files must be updated to resolve session-scoped paths:

| Hook | Currently Reads | Should Read |
|------|----------------|-------------|
| `context-injection.ts` | `state/todo.json` | `sessions/active/<id>/todo.json` |
| `context-injection.ts` | `state/health-metrics.json` | `sessions/active/<id>/health-metrics.json` |
| `context-injection.ts` | `state/runtime-profile.json` | `sessions/active/<id>/runtime-profile.json` |
| `session-lifecycle.ts` | `state/brain.json` | `sessions/active/<id>/brain.json` |
| `messages-transform.ts` | `state/brain.json` | `sessions/active/<id>/brain.json` |
| `gx-entry-guard.sh` | `state/enforcement.json` | `sessions/active/<id>/enforcement.json` |
| `gx-health-compute.sh` | `state/health-metrics.json` | `sessions/active/<id>/health-metrics.json` |

**The `sessionId` is available** in most hooks via `input.sessionID` (verified in `session-lifecycle.ts`). For bash scripts, it can be passed as an argument.

### Migration Strategy (Non-Breaking)

```
Phase A: Add getSessionPaths() to paths.ts (additive, no breakage)
Phase B: Create session directories on session.created event (additive)  
Phase C: Copy global state → session state on first use (backward compat)
Phase D: Switch hooks to prefer session-scoped paths with global fallback
Phase E: Deprecate global state/*.json writes (only session-scoped writes)
Phase F: Remove global fallback (breaking, major version)
```

**We stop at Phase D for now** — this gives us concurrency isolation with backward compatibility.

---

## RISK MATRIX

| Risk | Probability | Impact | Mitigation |
|------|------------|--------|------------|
| Agent guard reads stale `brain.json` agent field | Medium | Session runs with wrong injection system | Fallback: if agent unresolvable, fire BOTH (current behavior) |
| Session directory not created before hooks fire | Low | FileNotFound errors | Create dir synchronously in `session.created` event, before any hook |
| Backward compat break for scripts expecting global paths | Medium | Scripts fail silently | Phase D: session-scoped with global fallback |
| `hierarchy.json` concurrent writes during tree mutation | Low (current behavior) | Already exists — cursor pattern reduces frequency | Cursor pattern reduces shared writes to tree-structure-only |
