<thinking>
The user wants me to surface my reasoning for each decision, explain why it's the best choice, and then present all three decisions together. Let me think through each one deeply.

### Question 1: Execution Order (Fix 2 → Fix 1 → Fix 3)

The proposed order is: Staleness → Decoupling → Concurrency (increasing blast radius).

**Why this is the best order:**

1. **Fix 2 (Relational Staleness) first**: This is a single bash script replacement. It has ZERO upstream dependencies — no hook reads its output until `gx-health-compute.sh` calls it, and health-compute itself is called every 10 tool calls. Changing it doesn't break any chain. But it IMMEDIATELY stops the wall-clock time-bomb from poisoning health scores. If we fix the injection system (Fix 1) first but leave staleness broken, the injected context would still contain garbage health scores computed from wall-clock math. Fix the data quality first, then fix the delivery channel.

2. **Fix 1 (Decoupling) second**: Once staleness scoring is relational, we can safely decouple the injection systems. If we did concurrency (Fix 3) before decoupling, we'd be creating session-scoped paths that BOTH injection systems still write to simultaneously — meaning the cross-contamination just moves from global to session-level. The dual-injection conflict must be resolved before session isolation makes sense.

3. **Fix 3 (Concurrency) last**: This is the highest blast radius (10+ files, schema migration). It depends on both previous fixes being stable. If injection is still dual and staleness is still wall-clock, session-scoping just creates MORE wrong files in MORE directories.

**Why alternatives are worse:**
- Fix 1 first → Decoupled injection still feeds on garbage staleness scores
- Fix 3 first → Session-scoped state still cross-contaminated by dual injection
- Fix 1+2 simultaneously → Two moving parts make debugging harder, violates atomic-node principle

**VERDICT: Fix 2 → Fix 1 → Fix 3 is the correct order. Approve as-is.**

### Question 2: Agent Resolution Method

**Option A: Read brain.json** is the best choice.

**Why:**

1. **Already in the data path**: `session-lifecycle.ts` already reads state downstream (config.json at line 98). Adding a brain.json read at the top is consistent with the existing pattern. The file is already in `.hivemind/state/` and is updated every turn by `soft-governance.ts` and `event-handler.ts`.

2. **No external dependencies**: Option B (SDK enhancement) requires changing the OpenCode SDK itself — a dependency we don't control. The SDK's hook input interface (`{ sessionID?, model? }`) is defined by the platform. Changing it means submitting a PR to OpenCode, waiting for review, and updating our dependency. This adds weeks of latency to a critical fix.

3. **No new dependencies**: Option C (Session API) introduces a new runtime dependency on the OpenCode session API. If the API is unavailable, the hook fails. Brain.json is a local file — no network, no API, no latency.

4. **Sync-safe**: `brain.json` can be read synchronously with `readFileSync()` at the top of the hook, before any async work. This means the agent guard fires immediately, before any other injection logic runs. Options B and C would require async resolution, adding complexity to the guard.

5. **Graceful fallback**: If brain.json is missing (first-ever session, corrupted state), the `resolveCurrentAgent()` function returns `"unknown"`, and the guard falls through to fire BOTH systems (current behavior). No breakage.

**Why others are worse:**
- Option B: External dependency on SDK team; changes OpenCode's public API surface; multi-week timeline
- Option C: Network dependency; latency on every turn; failure mode if API unavailable; overkill for a string lookup

**Risk of Option A**: If brain.json's `session.agent` field is stale (e.g., set to "hiveminder" from a previous session but current session is "hivefiver"), the wrong injection system fires. **Mitigation**: The `session.created` event handler in `events.ts` already updates brain.json with the current session metadata. We add an assertion: if `brain.json.session.id` doesn't match `input.sessionID`, treat agent as "unknown" and fall through.

**VERDICT: Option A — Read brain.json.**

### Question 3: Concurrency Depth

**Phase A-D (Recommended)** is the best choice.

**Why:**

1. **Concurrency safety achieved**: After Phase D, each session reads from its own isolated state directory. Session A's `todo.json` is independent of Session B's. The cross-contamination vector is eliminated.

2. **Backward compatibility preserved**: Phase D includes a global fallback. If a session directory doesn't exist (e.g., old session format, external scripts), the hooks fall back to global `state/`. This means existing workflows, scripts, and tools that reference global paths continue to work.

3. **No breaking changes**: Phase E-F deprecate and remove global state — that's a major version change. It requires updating every script, tool, and reference that hardcodes `.hivemind/state/brain.json`. That's Node 2-3 territory, not Node 1.

4. **Incremental verification**: After Phase D, we can run concurrent sessions and VERIFY isolation works before committing to the full migration. If something breaks, we still have the global fallback.

5. **Platform restart manageable**: Phases A-D require ~3 restart cycles (after paths.ts change, after event handler change, after hook consumer changes). Phase E-F would require a full migration script plus coordinated restarts across all agents — too risky for a first pass.

**Why others are worse:**
- Phase A-B only: Creates the directories and adds paths, but hooks still read from global state. Concurrency is NOT actually fixed — just prepared. The user explicitly identified multi-session concurrency as a non-negotiable. A-B alone doesn't deliver it.
- Phase A-F (Full): Removes backward compatibility. Any external tool or script that reads `.hivemind/state/brain.json` breaks. We haven't audited all consumers yet. This is the correct eventual target but premature for Node 1.

**VERDICT: Phase A-D — Session-scoped with global fallback.**
</thinking>

# 🧠 DECISION RATIONALE DOCUMENT
## Three Architectural Decisions for Node 1

---

## DECISION 1: Execution Order — **Fix 2 → Fix 1 → Fix 3 (Approve as-is)**

### The Reasoning Chain

The execution order must follow the **data-quality-first principle**: fix the data being injected BEFORE fixing the delivery channel, and fix the delivery channel BEFORE scaling it to multi-session.

**Why Fix 2 (Relational Staleness) must come first:**

The staleness signal feeds into `gx-health-compute.sh`, which writes `health-metrics.json`, which is read by `context-injection.ts` and injected into **every LLM turn**. Right now, a 10-minute coffee break produces `score=0` ("CRITICAL DRIFT"), which cascades into:
- Health signals injected as "degraded" → LLM panics and role-drifts
- If we fix the delivery channel first (Fix 1) but leave staleness broken, we'd have a perfectly isolated injection system… delivering perfectly wrong data

This is analogous to fixing a broken water pipe (Fix 1) while the water supply itself is contaminated (Fix 2). Fix the source first.

**Single script, zero upstream dependencies, zero blast radius** — the ideal first move.

**Why Fix 1 (Decoupling) must come second:**

If we attempt session-scoping (Fix 3) before decoupling, we create session-scoped directories where **both** injection systems still write simultaneously. The cross-contamination simply moves from global-level to session-level. We'd be isolating rooms in a building where two competing HVAC systems still pump conflicting air into every room.

Decouple first → then the session-scoped state only has ONE system writing to it per session type.

**Why Fix 3 (Concurrency) must come last:**

Highest blast radius (10+ files, schema migration, path resolution changes). It depends on both previous fixes being stable. If either Fix 1 or Fix 2 introduces a regression, Fix 3 amplifies it across multiple session directories. With the other two fixes proven stable, Fix 3 becomes a clean infrastructure expansion rather than a risky refactor-during-chaos.

**Why alternatives are worse:**
- Fix 1 first → Cleanly decoupled channels still deliver garbage staleness data
- Fix 3 first → Multi-session isolation with dual-injection still firing = same conflict, more directories
- Parallel execution → Two moving parts make root-cause analysis impossible if something breaks; violates the "never attempt a one-shot fix" principle from the master directive

---

## DECISION 2: Agent Resolution — **Option A: Read brain.json**

### The Reasoning Chain

The core requirement is simple: when `session-lifecycle.ts` fires on a turn, it needs to know "am I in a hivefiver session?" to decide whether to mute itself.

**Why Option A (brain.json) is the strongest:**

1. **Zero external dependencies**: `brain.json` is a local file at `.hivemind/state/brain.json`. No network calls, no SDK version requirements, no API availability concerns. In a system already suffering from "false emitters," adding a new external dependency (SDK or API) would introduce a new failure mode into the most critical path.

2. **Already in the data flow**: `session-lifecycle.ts` already calls `loadConfig(directory)` at line 98 to read `config.json` from the same `.hivemind/` directory. Adding a `brain.json` read is architecturally consistent — same directory, same pattern, same error handling.

3. **Synchronous guard is possible**: `readFileSync(brainPath)` can resolve the agent name *before* any async injection logic runs. This means the mute decision happens at the very top of the function — if the agent is `hivefiver`, we return immediately with zero wasted computation. Options B and C require async resolution, meaning the hook must enter its async execution path before it can decide to bail.

4. **Graceful degradation**: If `brain.json` is missing (first session ever, corrupted state), `resolveCurrentAgent()` returns `"unknown"`, and the guard falls through — both systems fire (current behavior). No breakage. No crash. The worst case is "behavior unchanged from today."

5. **Session-ID cross-validation**: We add a safety assertion: if `brain.json.session.id !== input.sessionID`, treat the agent as `"unknown"`. This prevents a stale brain.json (from a previous session) from incorrectly muting the hook. The stale-agent risk is the primary attack vector against this approach, and this assertion neutralizes it.

**Why Options B and C are weaker:**

| Factor | Option B (SDK) | Option C (API) |
|--------|---------------|----------------|
| **Dependency** | OpenCode SDK team must accept & ship a PR | OpenCode session API must be running |
| **Timeline** | Weeks (external team review) | Days (new integration) |
| **Failure mode** | If SDK upgrade breaks, ALL hooks break | If API unavailable, hook fails open or closed |
| **Complexity** | Changes OpenCode's public hook input interface — breaking change for all plugins | New async dependency in synchronous-preferred guard path |
| **Principle fit** | Violates "constrain itself from SDK-oriented" per user directive | Adds runtime dependency counter to "isolation and decoupling" goal |

The user's master directive explicitly states: *"hivefiver module → only maximize its implementations within combining the innate opencode concepts in advanced mode and its uses of plugins and custom tools — and constrain itself from the SDK and server's oriented."* Options B and C violate this constraint.

---

## DECISION 3: Concurrency Depth — **Phase A-D (Session-Scoped with Global Fallback)**

### The Reasoning Chain

The user identified multi-session concurrency as a **non-negotiable** architectural flaw. But the fix must be incremental — not a big-bang migration.

**Why Phase A-D is the sweet spot:**

1. **Delivers the actual fix**: After Phase D, hooks read from `sessions/active/<session_id>/todo.json` instead of `state/todo.json`. Two concurrent sessions → two isolated state directories → zero cross-contamination. The user's requirement is MET.

2. **Global fallback = safety net**: Phase D includes a fallback: if the session directory doesn't exist, hooks fall back to global `state/`. This means:
   - Existing CLI scripts that reference `state/brain.json` → still work
   - Old session formats → still work  
   - External tools (Repomix, git hooks, CI) → still work
   - The only NEW behavior is: if a session directory exists, prefer it

3. **Verifiable before commitment**: After Phase D, we can empirically test: open two terminal tabs, run two sessions, verify their `todo.json` files are independent. If it works → we have evidence to proceed to E-F. If it doesn't → the fallback means nothing is broken.

**Why Phase A-B only is insufficient:**

Phase A-B creates the path definitions and session directories but **does not change any hook consumers**. Hooks still read from global `state/`. This means:
- The directories exist but are empty
- Concurrency is NOT fixed — just prepared
- The user explicitly called this a non-negotiable → preparation without delivery doesn't meet the bar

**Why Phase A-F (Full) is premature:**

Phase E deprecates global writes. Phase F removes the global fallback entirely. This means:
- Every script in `gx-context-engine/scripts/` that reads `$WORKTREE/.hivemind/state/health-metrics.json` must be updated to accept `--session-id` and resolve session-scoped paths
- Every custom tool in `.opencode/tool/` that writes to `state/` must be updated
- External consumers we haven't audited (CI, pre-commit hooks, manual scripts) would break silently
- This is a **major version** change requiring a migration guide, deprecation period, and extensive testing

Phase A-F is the *correct eventual target* — but it's Node 3-4 territory, after we've verified the infrastructure through Phases A-D.

---

## CONSOLIDATED DECISIONS

| Decision | Choice | One-Line Rationale |
|----------|--------|--------------------|
| **Execution Order** | Fix 2 → Fix 1 → Fix 3 | Fix data quality → fix delivery channel → scale to multi-session |
| **Agent Resolution** | Option A: Read brain.json | Zero dependencies, synchronous guard, graceful fallback, consistent with existing patterns |
| **Concurrency Depth** | Phase A-D | Delivers concurrency isolation with backward-compatible fallback; verify before committing to full migration |

---

These three decisions are mutually reinforcing:
- **Fix 2** ensures correct data flows into the injection layer
- **Fix 1 + Option A** ensures only the correct system delivers that data per agent type
- **Fix 3 (A-D)** ensures concurrent sessions don't cross-contaminate the now-correct, now-decoupled state

Each decision minimizes blast radius while delivering the user's non-negotiable requirements. Each includes a fallback path if something goes wrong. Each can be verified independently before proceeding to the next.

## Goal

The project uses the **OpenCode** platform (agents, commands, skills, plugins, custom tools, workflows) and has two competing subsystems:
- **System 1** (`.opencode/plugins/hiveops-governance/`) — the meta-framework plugin layer
- **System 2** (`src/hooks/`) — the product engine layer

  2. **Support multi-session concurrency** — State files (`brain.json`, `todo.json`, `hierarchy.json`) are global singletons. Multiple concurrent OpenCode sessions cross-contaminate. State must be session-scoped

## Discoveries

### Critical Root Cause: Dual-Injection Conflict
Two independent auto-injection systems fire on every LLM turn, unaware of each other:

| System | Files | Channel | Agent-Aware? |
|--------|-------|---------|-------------|
| System 1 (Plugin) | `context-injection.ts` | `output.messages[]` prepend | PARTIAL (hivefiver block only) |
| System 2a (Engine) | `session-lifecycle.ts` | `output.system[]` append | NO |
| System 2b (Engine) | `messages-transform.ts` | `output.messages[].parts[]` synthetic | NO |

Both read `hierarchy.json` but format/interpret it differently → contradictory hierarchy views in same context window.

### Hook Firing Frequency
- `context-injection.ts` — **EVERY turn**, reads 6 state files, injects system message
- `session-lifecycle.ts` — **EVERY turn**, reads 5 state files, injects `<hivemind>` block
- `messages-transform.ts` — **EVERY turn**, PREPEND anchors + APPEND checklist
- `delegation.ts` — **EVERY tool call** (before: `gx-enforce.sh`, after: `gx-health-compute.sh` every 10th)
- `soft-governance.ts` — **EVERY tool call**, writes counters read next turn
- 12 signal scripts fire every 10 tool calls via `gx-health-compute.sh`

### Staleness Time-Bomb
`gx-signal-hierarchy-freshness.sh` uses `score = clamp(100 - (age_minutes × 10), 0, 100)`. Score hits **ZERO at 10 minutes** of inactivity. A coffee break = "CRITICAL DRIFT" triggering false alerts.

### No Session Scoping
`src/lib/paths.ts` defines ALL paths as project-global. No `session_id` in any path. `getActiveSessionPath()` resolves dynamically but state files (`brain.json`, `todo.json`, `hierarchy.json`) are singletons.

### Injection Channel Separation
- System 1 injects via: `output.messages[]` (message-level prepend)
- System 2a injects via: `output.system[]` (system prompt)
- System 2b injects via: `output.messages[].parts[]` (synthetic parts within messages)
- They inject through DIFFERENT channels into the SAME context window

### Agent Awareness Gap
Only `context-injection.ts` has partial agent awareness (lines 294-330: hivefiver-specific blindness enforcement block checking `state.current.agent === "hivefiver"`). All other hooks inject universally regardless of agent.

### 10 Conflict Surfaces (from Team B)
1. `hivefiver-prime` ↔ `hivemind-governance` — both claim "load first"
2. `hivefiver.md` ↔ `hivefiver-start.md` — root router vs specific stage
3. `gx-health-compute.sh` ↔ `health-metrics.json` — race condition
4. `route-stage.sh` ↔ `hierarchy.json` — concurrent mutations
5. `context-injection.ts` ↔ 5 state files — stale = poisoned
6. `runtime-gate.sh` ↔ `gx-mid-guard.sh` — duplicate enforcement
7. `hivefiver.md blindness` ↔ `context-injection.ts blindness` — DOUBLE ENFORCEMENT
8. `hivefiver-vibecoder.yaml` ↔ `enterprise-architect.yaml` — routing collision
9. `STATE.md` ↔ `hierarchy.json` — DUAL SOURCE OF TRUTH
10. `context-integrity` ↔ `context-quality-escalation` — deprecated but exists

### Delegation Topology (hardcoded in types.ts)
- hivefiver can delegate to: `[hivexplorer, hiverd, hiveplanner]` (maxDepth: 2)
- hivexplorer and hiverd are TERMINAL (maxDepth: 0, cannot delegate)
- Mismatch: plugin topology doesn't match agent `.md` profile delegation lists

### State Mutation Architecture
- Hooks are CQRS-compliant (read-only, queue mutations via `queueStateMutation()`)
- Tools own writes via `flushMutations(stateManager)`
- Exception: `hivemind-cycle.ts` bypasses queue with direct `stateManager.save()`
- Mutation queue max: 100 items, FIFO overflow

## 2. Session Hierarchy Awareness

Detect your session type BEFORE acting:

| Signal | You are in... | Behavior |
|--------|---------------|----------|

| **Complexity** | Single-node (1 file) vs. Multi-node (cross-file) vs. Systemic (cross-domain) | Whether to delegate |
| **Context Quality** | Clean vs. Stale vs. Poisoned | Whether to proceed or collect |

**Coordinator-fronted** (DEFAULT for hivefiver in main session):
- Broad view, hierarchy-level context
- Outline frames and skeletons, NOT branch-level detail
- Delegation NOT execution
- Treat outlines as iterative bibles

**Executor-fronted** (ONLY for short, non-project tasks):
- Detail-level planning with granular tasks

- Complete only when full evidence collected

**Researcher-fronted** (ONLY in sub-sessions):
- Swarm-oriented, multi-source

## 5. Context Guardrails

### Escalation Levels (by turn count approximation)

| Level | Signal | Tone | Action |
|-------|--------|------|--------|
| **L1 — Mild** (early session) | Context is clean, work is focused | Instructive, guideline | Remind of hierarchy and progressive disclosure |
| **L2 — Alert** (mid session) | Multiple topics active, context branching | Urgent, corrective | Consolidate. Symlink knowledge. Stop loading new skills. |
| **L3 — Critical** (approaching limits) | Context rot signals: contradictions, repeated patterns, long outputs | Forceful, halting | Spawn sub-agent for context collection. Summarize what's done vs pending. |
| **L4 — Emergency** (near compact) | Model producing circular outputs, missing prior decisions | STOP | Emit handoff payload immediately. Do NOT continue work. |

### Rot Detection Signals

- You're repeating a decision you already made → L3
- You can't find a file you referenced 5 turns ago → L3
- Your output contradicts your earlier output → L4
- User is forcing completion but context is degraded → L3, push back with evidence

### SOT Validation Rules

Before trusting ANY file as Source of Truth:
1. Is it hierarchically structured? (in a grouped folder, not loose at root)
2. Does it NOT have a date-timestamp in the filename? (timestamped = branch, not SOT)
3. Is it connected to other artifacts? (disconnected = likely stale)
4. Is it recent and iteratively updated? (>48h without update = suspect)

If ANY check fails → treat as hypothesis, not truth.

## 7. OpenCode Platform Awareness

### Known Facts (verified this session via Context7 + DeepWiki):

**Agent frontmatter — machine-parsed fields:**
`description`, `mode`, `model`, `temperature`, `tools`, `permission`, `steps`, `hidden`

**Agent frontmatter — decorative (LLM reads, engine ignores):**
Any other YAML fields (e.g., `identity`, `scope`, `delegation_policy`) — harmless but not enforced by platform.

**Skill system:**
- Skills load on-demand via `skill({ name: "..." })` — never preloaded via frontmatter
- Skill content remains loaded in session state, but model attention to old skill text can decay across long turns
- Agent body loads ONCE at session init, NOT per-turn
- Discovery: CWD → git worktree → `.opencode/skills/` → `.claude/skills/` → `.agents/skills/` → global
- Up to 10 bundled files listed per skill directory

**Permission system:**
- Ruleset: ordered rules, last-match-wins with glob wildcards
- Actions: `allow`, `deny`, `ask`
- Categories: `read`, `edit` (covers edit+write+patch), `bash` (full command string), `task` (agent name), `skill` (skill name)
- Merge: defaults → user config → agent config → session overrides

**Session child isolation:**
- Child sessions (via TaskTool) get their own permission ruleset
- Default child permissions: `todowrite: deny`, `todoread: deny`, `task: deny`
- Skills don't inherit — each child loads fresh

### FILE 2: `node-1-proposal.md` (447 lines)

```markdown
---

# 🏗️ NODE 1 REFACTORING BLUEPRINT
## The Injection Layer — Decoupling, Concurrency & Relational Staleness

**Version**: 1.0-DRAFT  
**Date**: 2026-03-03  
**Author**: hivefiver (synthesized from Team A + Team B + Human Architect)  
**Status**: AWAITING APPROVAL — No file writes until approved

---

## EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

Three surgical fixes to the auto-injection layer, ordered by blast radius (smallest first):

| Fix | Target | Risk | Blast Radius |
|-----|--------|------|-------------|
| **Fix 1: Dual-Injection Decoupling** | `context-injection.ts` + `session-lifecycle.ts` + `messages-transform.ts` | 🟡 Medium | 3 files, no schema change |
| **Fix 2: Relational Staleness** | `gx-signal-hierarchy-freshness.sh` | 🟢 Low | 1 script, no upstream deps |
| **Fix 3: Session-Scoped State** | `paths.ts` + all hook consumers | 🔴 High | 10+ files, schema migration |

Execution order: **Fix 2 → Fix 1 → Fix 3** (increasing blast radius)

---

## FIX 1: DUAL-INJECTION DECOUPLING

### The Problem (Verified)

Two independent injection systems fire on **every LLM turn**, unaware of each other:

| System | File | Channel | Agent-Aware? | Session-Scoped? |
|--------|------|---------|-------------|-----------------|
| **System 1** (Meta/Plugin) | `context-injection.ts` | `output.messages[]` (prepend msg) | PARTIAL (hivefiver block) | NO |
| **System 2a** (Product/Engine) | `session-lifecycle.ts` | `output.system[]` (system prompt) | NO | PARTIAL (sessionID gate) |
| **System 2b** (Product/Engine) | `messages-transform.ts` | `output.messages[].parts[]` (synthetic parts) | NO | PARTIAL (Set gate) |

Both read `hierarchy.json`. Both inject hierarchy data. Different formats. **The LLM sees contradictory hierarchy views.**

### The Decoupling Strategy: Agent-Domain Routing

**Principle**: System 1 owns `hivefiver` sessions. System 2 owns all other agent sessions. Neither fires for the other's domain.

#### 1A. Modify `context-injection.ts` — Add Agent Guard
#### 1B. Modify `session-lifecycle.ts` — Add Inverse Agent Guard
#### 1C. Modify `messages-transform.ts` — Same Pattern
#### 1D. Resolve Conflict Surface #7: Double Blindness Enforcement
#### 1E. Resolve Conflict Surface #9: Dual SOT (STATE.md vs hierarchy.json)

---

## FIX 2: RELATIONAL STALENESS (Kill Wall-Clock)

### The Problem (Verified)

`gx-signal-hierarchy-freshness.sh` lines 89-97:
```bash
age_minutes=$((age_seconds / 60))
score=$((100 - (age_minutes * decay_rate)))
```

With default `decay_rate=10`, the score hits **ZERO after 10 minutes**. A coffee break = "CRITICAL DRIFT."

### The Fix: Sequential/Topological Freshness

**Replace time-based decay with three relational signals:**
- SIGNAL 1: Git Drift (0-40 points)
- SIGNAL 2: Row-Chain Continuity (0-35 points)
- SIGNAL 3: Session Continuity (0-25 points)

**Key change**: A developer sleeping for 8 hours scores **100** if no code changed and the hierarchy is internally consistent. A developer making 30 code commits while the hierarchy hasn't updated scores **25** even if it was updated 2 minutes ago.

---

## FIX 3: SESSION-SCOPED STATE (Multi-Concurrency)

### The Problem (Verified)

`paths.ts` defines **ALL** state paths as project-global:
```
.hivemind/state/brain.json      ← ONE global file
.hivemind/state/hierarchy.json  ← ONE global file
.hivemind/state/todo.json       ← ONE global file
```

Two concurrent sessions read/write the same files → cross-contamination.

### The Architecture: Layered State Isolation

**Principle**: Split state into **Project-Level** (shared, rare writes) and **Session-Level** (isolated, frequent writes).

```
.hivemind/
├── config.json                          # Project-level (shared, stable)
├── state/
│   ├── hierarchy.json                   # Project-level SOT (the tree itself)
│   └── sot-index.json                   # Project-level artifact registry
│
├── sessions/
│   ├── manifest.json                    # Session registry
│   ├── active/
│   │   ├── session-<id-1>/              # Session A's isolated state
│   │   │   ├── brain.json               # Session-scoped runtime state
│   │   │   ├── todo.json                # Session-scoped TODOs
│   │   │   ├── health-metrics.json      # Session-scoped health
│   │   │   ├── runtime-profile.json     # Session-scoped profile
│   │   │   ├── enforcement.json         # Session-scoped enforcement
│   │   │   ├── context-recovery.json    # Session-scoped recovery
│   │   │   └── cursor.json              # Session's pointer into hierarchy.json
│   │   │
│   │   └── session-<id-2>/              # Session B's isolated state
│   │       ├── brain.json
│   │       ├── todo.json
│   │       └── ...
│   │
│   └── archive/                         # Completed sessions
```

### Migration Path in `paths.ts`

```typescript
// NEW: Session-scoped path resolution
export function getSessionPaths(
  projectRoot: string,
  sessionId: string
): SessionScopedPaths { ... }
```

### Migration Strategy (Non-Breaking)

```
Phase A: Add getSessionPaths() to paths.ts (additive, no breakage)
Phase B: Create session directories on session.created event (additive)  
Phase C: Copy global state → session state on first use (backward compat)
Phase D: Switch hooks to prefer session-scoped paths with global fallback
Phase E: Deprecate global state/*.json writes (only session-scoped writes)
Phase F: Remove global fallback (breaking, major version)
```

**We stop at Phase D for now** — this gives us concurrency isolation with backward compatibility.

---

## EXECUTION SEQUENCING

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ NODE 1: INJECTION LAYER REFACTORING                      │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                          │
│  Step 1: Fix 2 (Relational Staleness)     ← LOWEST RISK │
│  ├── Modify: gx-signal-hierarchy-freshness.sh            │
│  ├── Test: Run signal script, verify scoring             │
│  └── Gate: health-metrics.json shows relational scores   │
│          ↓                                               │
│  Step 2: Fix 1 (Dual-Injection Decoupling) ← MEDIUM     │
│  ├── Modify: context-injection.ts (add agent guard)      │
│  ├── Modify: session-lifecycle.ts (add inverse guard)    │
│  ├── Modify: messages-transform.ts (add inverse guard)   │
│  ├── Test: Start hivefiver session → verify ONLY Sys1    │
│  ├── Test: Start hivemaker session → verify ONLY Sys2    │
│  └── Gate: No double-injection in any agent session      │
│          ↓                                               │
│  Step 3: Fix 3A-D (Session-Scoped State)  ← HIGHEST     │
│  ├── Modify: paths.ts (add getSessionPaths)              │
│  ├── Modify: events.ts (create session dir on start)     │
│  ├── Modify: all hooks (session-scoped reads)            │
│  ├── Modify: all gx scripts (accept session_id arg)     │
│  ├── Test: Two concurrent sessions → no cross-write     │
│  └── Gate: State isolation verified                      │
│          ↓                                               │
│  ⚠️ PLATFORM RESTART REQUIRED after each Step            │
│                                                          │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

---

## RISK MATRIX

| Risk | Probability | Impact | Mitigation |
|------|------------|--------|------------|
| Agent guard reads stale `brain.json` agent field | Medium | Session runs with wrong injection system | Fallback: if agent unresolvable, fire BOTH |
| Session directory not created before hooks fire | Low | FileNotFound errors | Create dir synchronously in session.created event |
| Backward compat break for scripts expecting global paths | Medium | Scripts fail silently | Phase D: session-scoped with global fallback |
| `hierarchy.json` concurrent writes during tree mutation | Low | Already exists — cursor pattern reduces frequency | Cursor pattern reduces shared writes |

---

## WHAT THIS BLUEPRINT DOES NOT COVER (Future Nodes)

| Deferred Item | Why Deferred | Future Node |
|---------------|-------------|-------------|
| Fixing hivefiver-prime SKILL.md content | Content changes AFTER injection layer is stable | Node 2 |
| Resolving 10 conflict surfaces from Team B | Infrastructure must be clean first | Node 2-3 |
| Skills refactoring (find-skill, skill-creator audit) | Depends on clean injection context | Node 3 |
| Command/Workflow restructuring | Depends on working skills | Node 4 |
| Stub script completion (gx-semantic-validate, gx-swarm-launch) | Not urgent — stubs don't inject | Node 5 |

**Output:**
```
<skill_content name="hivefiver-mode">
# Skill: hivefiver-mode

# Hivefiver Mode Routing

Determine current stage and route to correct command + workflow + references.

## Stage Detection

Determine stage using one of two paths:

1) If bash is allowed, run `scripts/route-stage.sh` directly.

```bash
./scripts/route-stage.sh /Users/apple/hivemind-plugin
```

2) If bash is denied (common for hivefiver), delegate to `hivexplorer` and request the script output JSON with evidence.

The script reads:
- `.hivemind/state/hierarchy.json` — Trajectory → Tactic → Action tree
- `.hivemind/hive-modules/hivefiver-v2/STATE.md` — Module state (if exists)

Output JSON:
```json
{
  "stage": "spec",
  "command": "/hivefiver spec",
  "workflow": ".opencode/workflows/hivefiver-spec.yaml",
  "refs": ["references/opencode-asset-authoring.md"]
}
```

## Stage → Command Mapping

| Stage | Command | Workflow | Primary Reference |
|-------|---------|----------|-------------------|
| `start` | `/hivefiver start` | `hivefiver-start.yaml` | governance-rules.md |
| `intake` | `/hivefiver intake` | `hivefiver-intake.yaml` | governance-rules.md |
| `spec` | `/hivefiver spec` | `hivefiver-spec.yaml` | asset-contracts.md |
| `architect` | `/hivefiver architect` | `hivefiver-architect.yaml` | asset-contracts.md |
| `build` | `/hivefiver build` | `hivefiver-build.yaml` | asset-contracts.md |
| `audit` | `/hivefiver audit` | `hivefiver-audit.yaml` | completion-criteria.md |
| `doctor` | `/hivefiver doctor` | `hivefiver-doctor.yaml` | completion-criteria.md |

## Progressive Disclosure Rules

Load references by depth:

- **L0**: Always present — skill name + description
- **L1**: On invoke — SKILL.md body (~500-2K tokens)
- **L2**: On complexity > 2 — domain references (~1K-5K)
- **L3**: Audit mode only — full reference bundle

## SOT Parent-Down Walk Algorithm

1. Read hierarchy.json root.trajectory.content
2. Walk: trajectory → tactic → action
3. Find deepest action with status !== "complete"
4. Map action content to stage keyword
5. If no match → default to `start`

## Self-Delegation Checkpoint Pattern

When stage requires continuation beyond current context:

1. Emit checkpoint: current stage, completed gates, next action
2. Self-delegate with mode = next stage
3. Preserve loaded skills across delegation

```yaml
delegation_packet:
  objective: "Continue from stage X to stage Y"
  in_scope_paths: [".opencode/skills/hivefiver-mode/**"]
  constraints: ["preserve loaded skills", "no recursive delegation"]
  required_outputs: ["stage_advance", "evidence"]
```

## Session-Based Delegation

For clean-context delegation, compose an `opencode run` command from route-stage output.
Use this direct shell path only when bash is explicitly allowed in the session.
In default blind mode, request `hivexplorer` evidence for stage routing and delegate without local shell execution.

```bash
# Get stage routing
ROUTE=$(./scripts/route-stage.sh "$(pwd)")
STAGE=$(echo "$ROUTE" | jq -r '.stage')
COMMAND=$(echo "$ROUTE" | jq -r '.command')

# Compose parsed prompt as workflow instruction
PROMPT="Load hivefiver-prime first, then hivefiver-mode.
Current stage: $STAGE
Execute: $COMMAND
Constraints: stay in .opencode/** and .hivemind/** only.
Then load only the stage helper skill (hivefiver-coordination when gate checks are required).
Quality gate: run quality-check.sh $STAGE before claiming completion."

# Delegate with clean session
opencode run --agent hivefiver --title "hivefiver:stage:$STAGE" "$PROMPT"
```

### Parsed Prompt Composition

The prompt IS the workflow instruction. Compose from:

1. **Skill loading directives** — which skills to load first
2. **Stage context** — current stage from SOT
3. **Command to execute** — the mapped command
4. **Constraints** — scope boundaries, permission limits
5. **Quality gate** — what to verify before completion
6. **Parent context** — 2-3 line summary from current session

### Permission Constraint Templates

Per-stage permission rulesets:

| Stage | Allowed Edits | Denied Edits | Task Delegation |
|-------|--------------|--------------|-----------------|
| start | `.hivemind/**` | `.opencode/**`, `src/**` | hivefiver only |
| intake | `.hivemind/**` | `.opencode/**`, `src/**` | hivefiver only |
| spec | `.hivemind/**`, `docs/**` | `.opencode/**`, `src/**` | hivefiver only |
| architect | `.opencode/**`, `.hivemind/**` | `src/**` | hivefiver only |
| build | `.opencode/**` | `src/**`, `tests/**` | hivefiver only |
| audit | none (read-only) | `*` | hivefiver only |
| doctor | `.opencode/**`, `.hivemind/**` | `src/**` | hivefiver only |

## Fallback Behavior

If SOT unreadable → output:
```json
{ "stage": "start", "command": "/hivefiver", "workflow": null, "refs": [] }

## Execution Protocol

1. Load this skill after `hivefiver-prime`
2. Obtain stage route JSON (direct bash OR delegated `hivexplorer` evidence)
3. Parse route output and determine stage
4. Load only the helper skill required for that stage (usually one)
5. Execute or self-delegate based on stage requirements
6. Before claiming completion, verify stage outputs through `hivexplorer`
7. For pipeline-closing stages, ensure handoff/export artifact is created

### Runtime Enforcement Rationale

Forensic audit of session `ses_356f` (10,668 lines) proved that without mandatory runtime-gate invocation, agents skip ALL enforcement 100% of the time — 14 scripts existed, 12 were never executed, zero quality gates ran. The runtime-gate.sh is the unified enforcer that prevents this failure mode.

## 5. ARCHITECTURAL CONCERNS

### 5.1 Dual-State Architecture

The system maintains **TWO** parallel state hierarchies:

1. **brain.json** (`src/hooks/` consumers)
   - TypeScript-based hooks
   - CQRS-compliant mutation queue
   - Session-scoped lifecycle

2. **`.hivemind/state/`** (GX-Pack consumers)
   - Bash scripts
   - Direct file I/O
   - Turn-scoped health computation

**Risk**: These can diverge. Example: `hierarchy.*` exists in both `brain.json` and `.hivemind/state/hierarchy.json`. If one is updated without the other, context injection will be inconsistent.

### 5.2 Orphan Field Accumulation

The schema has accumulated write-only fields that were added for features but never integrated into context injection:

- `ratings` — Appears to be self-rating feature never completed
- `memory_governance.classified_counts` — Classification tracking without consumer
- `complexity_nudge_shown` — Nudge feature without read path

## EVIDENCE 3: `/Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/src/hooks/event-handler.ts` (418 lines)

### Session Event Handling (Lines 180-225):

```typescript
switch (event.type) {
  case "session.created":
    await log.info(`[event] session.created: ${(event as EventSessionCreated).properties.info.id}`)
    break

  case "session.idle":
    await log.info(`[event] session.idle: ${(event as EventSessionIdle).properties.sessionID}`)

    if (!state) {
      await log.debug("[event] session.idle skipped (no brain state)")
      break
    }

    let nextState = state
    
    // V3.0: Increment user_turn_count on each user→assistant→user cycle
    nextState = {
      ...nextState,
      metrics: {
        ...nextState.metrics,
        user_turn_count: nextState.metrics.user_turn_count + 1,
      },
    }
    
    const staleness = getStalenessInfo(nextState, config.stale_session_days)

    // CQRS FIX: Queue mutation instead of direct save (hook is read-only)
    queueStateMutation({
      type: "UPDATE_METRICS",
      payload: { metrics: nextState.metrics },
      source: "event-handler.session.idle",
    })
    break
```

**GAP IDENTIFIED**: `session.created` event ONLY logs — no session directory creation happens here. This is where session-scoped directory initialization should occur.

| Function | Purpose | Lines |

| `clearMutationQueue()` | Clear queue without applying | 591-595 |
| `deepMerge(target, source)` | Deep merge helper | 607-650 |

### CQRS Flow (Lines 10-18):
```typescript
/**
 * Problem: Hooks should be read-only (CQRS principle), but some hooks
 * need to update state (e.g., metrics, hierarchy). Direct stateManager.save()
 * calls from hooks violate CQRS.
 *
 * Solution: Hooks push mutations to this queue instead of writing directly.
 * Tools (write operations) flush the queue and apply mutations.
 */
```

**CRITICAL FOR SESSION SCOPING**: Any session-scoped path must integrate with this queue system. The queue is module-scoped (global within process), so session-scoped mutations would need either:
1. Session-scoped queues, OR
2. Session ID embedded in mutation payloads

## INVESTIGATION SUMMARY

### Gaps Identified for Session-Scoped State Isolation:

| Gap | Location | Impact |
|-----|----------|--------|
| **No session-scoped paths in HivemindPaths** | `paths.ts` | All paths are project-scoped |
| **session.created does not create session directories** | `event-handler.ts:180-182` | Only logs, no initialization |
| **Manifest empty but session files exist** | `.hivemind/sessions/manifest.json` | Desynchronization risk |
| **State mutation queue is global** | `state-mutation-queue.ts` | No session isolation in queue |
| **No session-scoped state directory** | `sessions/active/` | Session files exist but no state subdirs |
| **Brain state shared across sessions** | `state/brain.json` | Single file for all session runtime state |

### Recommended Path Additions for Session Scoping:

```typescript
// In HivemindPaths interface:
sessionScopedDir: string        // sessions/active/<session-id>/
sessionScopedState: string      // sessions/active/<session-id>/state.json
sessionScopedMetrics: string    // sessions/active/<session-id>/metrics.json
sessionScopedCycleLog: string   // sessions/active/<session-id>/cycle-log.json
```

### Integration Points Required:

1. **event-handler.ts** — `session.created` → create session-scoped directory
2. **state-mutation-queue.ts** — Add session ID to mutation payloads
3. **paths.ts** — Add `getSessionScopedPaths(projectRoot, sessionId)` function
4. **persistence.ts** — Load/save from session-scoped paths when session active

## Task 1: Profile Generation Script (gx-entry-guard.sh)

**File**: `/Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/.opencode/skills/gx-context-engine/scripts/gx-entry-guard.sh`

**Lines 1-235 (COMPLETE FILE)**:

```bash
#!/usr/bin/env bash
# gx-entry-guard.sh — Session entry: build runtime profile, verify policy, lock state
#
# CHAIN: Session Entry (Chain 1) — Step 1
# TRIGGER: Command invocation (!`cmd` pre-prompt injection)
# OUTPUT: .hivemind/state/runtime-profile.json
#
# Algorithm:
#   1. CLASSIFY INTENT (reuse classify-intent.sh if available, else basic)
#   2. RESOLVE ROLE ENVELOPE (intent → primary/secondary/monitor mapping)
#   3. COMPUTE CAPABILITIES (from delegation topology)
#   4. BUILD PROFILE ID (deterministic hash)
#   5. PERSIST + validate
#   6. LOCK STATE (mark profile active)
#
# Determinism: identical inputs → identical profile ID (sha256 of intent+scope+policy)

set -euo pipefail

WORKDIR="${1:-.}"
INTENT_HINT="${2:-}"
POLICY_VERSION="gx-pack-v1"

STATE_DIR="$WORKDIR/.hivemind/state"
PROFILE_FILE="$STATE_DIR/runtime-profile.json"
HIERARCHY_FILE="$STATE_DIR/hierarchy.json"
ENFORCEMENT_FILE="$STATE_DIR/enforcement.json"
TODO_FILE="$STATE_DIR/todo.json"

# Ensure state directory exists
mkdir -p "$STATE_DIR"

# ── Step 1: CLASSIFY INTENT ──

classify_intent() {
  local hint="$1"

  # If hint provided, use it directly
  if [ -n "$hint" ]; then
    case "$hint" in
      build_new|fix_broken|audit_health|extend|improve)
        echo "$hint"
        return
        ;;
    esac
  fi

  # Try to use classify-intent.sh from hivefiver-mode
  local classifier="$WORKDIR/.opencode/skills/hivefiver-mode/scripts/classify-intent.sh"
  if [ -x "$classifier" ] && [ -n "$hint" ]; then
    local result
    result=$(bash "$classifier" "$hint" 2>/dev/null || echo '{"intent":"build_new"}')
    echo "$result" | jq -r '.intent // "build_new"' 2>/dev/null || echo "build_new"
    return
  fi

  # Default
  echo "build_new"
}

INTENT=$(classify_intent "$INTENT_HINT")

# ── Step 2: RESOLVE ROLE ENVELOPE ──

resolve_envelope() {
  local intent="$1"
  case "$intent" in
    build_new)
      echo '{"primary":{"agent":"hiveminder","level":2},"secondary":{"agent":"hivemaker","level":3},"monitor":{"agent":"hiveq","level":3}}'
      ;;
    fix_broken)
      echo '{"primary":{"agent":"hiveminder","level":2},"secondary":{"agent":"hivehealer","level":3},"monitor":{"agent":"hiveq","level":3}}'
      ;;
    audit_health)
      echo '{"primary":{"agent":"hiveq","level":2},"secondary":{"agent":"hivexplorer","level":3},"monitor":{"agent":"hiveminder","level":3}}'
      ;;
    extend|improve)
      echo '{"primary":{"agent":"hiveminder","level":2},"secondary":{"agent":"hivemaker","level":3},"monitor":{"agent":"hiveq","level":3}}'
      ;;
    *)
      echo '{"primary":{"agent":"hiveminder","level":2},"secondary":{"agent":"hivexplorer","level":3},"monitor":{"agent":"hiveq","level":3}}'
      ;;
  esac
}

ENVELOPE=$(resolve_envelope "$INTENT")

# ── Step 3: COMPUTE CAPABILITIES ──

compute_capabilities() {
  local intent="$1"
  local envelope="$2"
  local secondary
  secondary=$(echo "$envelope" | jq -r '.secondary.agent')
  local depth_limit
  depth_limit=$(echo "$envelope" | jq -r '.primary.level + 1')

  # Base tools available to all
  local tools='["read","glob","grep","task","skill","hiveops_todo","hiveops_gate","hiveops_sot","hiveops_export"]'

  # Scope based on intent
  local paths
  case "$intent" in
    audit_health)
      paths='[".opencode/**",".hivemind/**","docs/**"]'
      ;;
    *)
      paths='[".opencode/**",".hivemind/**","docs/**"]'
      ;;
  esac

  # Delegate list from secondary + monitor + hivexplorer
  local delegates
  delegates=$(echo "$envelope" | jq -c '[.secondary.agent, .monitor.agent, "hivexplorer"] | unique')

  jq -n \
    --argjson tools "$tools" \
    --argjson paths "$paths" \
    --argjson depth_limit "$depth_limit" \
    --argjson delegates "$delegates" \
    '{tools: $tools, paths: $paths, depth_limit: $depth_limit, delegate_to: $delegates}'
}

CAPABILITIES=$(compute_capabilities "$INTENT" "$ENVELOPE")

# ── Step 4: BUILD PROFILE ID (deterministic) ──

build_profile_id() {
  local intent="$1"
  local scope="$2"
  local policy="$3"
  local input="${intent}:${scope}:${policy}"

  if command -v sha256sum >/dev/null 2>&1; then
    echo "gx-profile-$(echo -n "$input" | sha256sum | head -c 12)"
  elif command -v shasum >/dev/null 2>&1; then
    echo "gx-profile-$(echo -n "$input" | shasum -a 256 | head -c 12)"
  else
    # Fallback: use md5
    echo "gx-profile-$(echo -n "$input" | md5 | head -c 12)"
  fi
}

SCOPE=$(echo "$CAPABILITIES" | jq -r '.paths | join(",")')
PROFILE_ID=$(build_profile_id "$INTENT" "$SCOPE" "$POLICY_VERSION")

# ── Step 5: CHECK EXISTING PROFILE ──

if [ -f "$PROFILE_FILE" ]; then
  EXISTING_ID=$(jq -r '.id // ""' "$PROFILE_FILE" 2>/dev/null || echo "")
  EXISTING_TTL=$(jq -r '.ttl // 0' "$PROFILE_FILE" 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
  EXISTING_CREATED=$(jq -r '.created_epoch // 0' "$PROFILE_FILE" 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
  NOW=$(date +%s)
  ELAPSED=$(( NOW - EXISTING_CREATED ))
  TTL_SECONDS=$(( EXISTING_TTL / 1000 ))

  if [ "$EXISTING_ID" = "$PROFILE_ID" ] && [ "$ELAPSED" -lt "$TTL_SECONDS" ]; then
    # Profile still valid
    echo "{\"status\":\"cached\",\"profile_id\":\"$PROFILE_ID\",\"ttl_remaining\":$(( TTL_SECONDS - ELAPSED ))}"
    exit 0
  fi
fi

# ── Step 6: BUILD CONSTRAINTS ──

build_constraints() {
  local intent="$1"
  local constraints='[]'

  # Universal constraints
  constraints=$(echo "$constraints" | jq '. + [
    "L3 agents cannot execute critical-path edits without delegation packet",
    "Monitor must verify before stage promotion",
    "All delegation packets must include profile_id"
  ]')

  # Intent-specific constraints
  case "$intent" in
    build_new)
      constraints=$(echo "$constraints" | jq '. + ["New assets must have contract compliance before write"]')
      ;;
    fix_broken)
      constraints=$(echo "$constraints" | jq '. + ["Fixes must not introduce new anti-patterns","Root cause must be identified before applying fix"]')
      ;;
    audit_health)
      constraints=$(echo "$constraints" | jq '. + ["Audit is read-only — no modifications allowed","Findings must be severity-ranked"]')
      ;;
  esac

  echo "$constraints"
}

CONSTRAINTS=$(build_constraints "$INTENT")

# ── Step 7: PERSIST PROFILE ──

NOW_ISO=$(date -u +"%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ")
NOW_EPOCH=$(date +%s)

jq -n \
  --arg id "$PROFILE_ID" \
  --arg created "$NOW_ISO" \
  --argjson created_epoch "$NOW_EPOCH" \
  --argjson ttl 3600000 \
  --arg intent "$INTENT" \
  --arg policy_version "$POLICY_VERSION" \
  --argjson role_envelope "$ENVELOPE" \
  --argjson capabilities "$CAPABILITIES" \
  --argjson constraints "$CONSTRAINTS" \
  '{
    id: $id,
    created: $created,
    created_epoch: $created_epoch,
    ttl: $ttl,
    intent: $intent,
    policy_version: $policy_version,
    role_envelope: $role_envelope,
    capabilities: $capabilities,
    constraints: $constraints
  }' > "$PROFILE_FILE"

# ── Step 8: LOCK STATE ──

# Update enforcement state with profile reference
if [ -f "$ENFORCEMENT_FILE" ]; then
  TMP_FILE=$(mktemp)
  jq --arg profile_id "$PROFILE_ID" \
     --arg intent "$INTENT" \
     '. + {active_profile: $profile_id, active_intent: $intent}' \
     "$ENFORCEMENT_FILE" > "$TMP_FILE" && mv "$TMP_FILE" "$ENFORCEMENT_FILE"
fi

# ── OUTPUT ──

echo "{\"status\":\"created\",\"profile_id\":\"$PROFILE_ID\",\"intent\":\"$INTENT\",\"policy\":\"$POLICY_VERSION\",\"ttl\":3600}"
```

**KEY MECHANISMS**:
- **Lines 65-84**: `resolve_envelope()` — Hardcoded intent→agent mapping
- **Lines 128-142**: `build_profile_id()` — Deterministic hash (sha256 of `intent:scope:policy`)
- **Lines 90-122**: `compute_capabilities()` — Derives tools/paths/delegations from envelope

## INVESTIGATION FINDINGS

### Determinism Mechanism:

1. **Profile ID Generation** (gx-entry-guard.sh:128-142):
   - Input: `${intent}:${scope}:${policy_version}`
   - Algorithm: SHA-256 hash (first 12 chars)
   - Example: `build_new:.opencode/**,.hivemind/**,docs/**:gx-pack-v1` → `gx-profile-2a0935eb57ce`

2. **Role Resolution** (gx-entry-guard.sh:65-84):
   - Intent classification determines agent envelope
   - Hardcoded mapping in `resolve_envelope()` function
   - No runtime lookups — purely algorithmic

3. **Capability Derivation** (gx-entry-guard.sh:90-122):
   - Tools: Fixed base set for all profiles
   - Paths: Intent-dependent but currently uniform
   - Delegates: Computed from envelope (secondary + monitor + hivexplorer)

### Schema Registry:

- **Location**: `.hivemind/state/schema-registry.json`
- **Validator**: `gx-schema-sync.sh` (bash-based, jq validation)
- **No TypeScript Schema**: Schema definitions are in bash scripts and markdown specs only

### Evidence Package Complete

All files read verbatim with line numbers. No interpretation. Full contents provided.
</task_result>

Now I have a CRITICAL finding from the runtime-profile investigation:

**The Profile Pattern has a FATAL GAP for our use case:**

The `runtime-profile.json` is generated by `gx-entry-guard.sh` which maps INTENT (build_new, fix_broken, audit_health) to a role_envelope. But the role_envelope resolves to agent ROLES (hiveminder, hivemaker, hiveq) based on what the WORK TYPE is — NOT based on which agent is CURRENTLY RUNNING in this session.

The `resolve_envelope()` function on lines 65-84 of gx-entry-guard.sh is hardcoded:
- build_new → primary: hiveminder, secondary: hivemaker
- fix_broken → primary: hiveminder, secondary: hivehealer
- audit_health → primary: hiveq, secondary: hivexplorer

But when we need to decouple hooks (Fix 1), we need to know: "Is the CURRENT session running as hivefiver?" The runtime-profile doesn't have a field for the current running agent — it has a field for the PLANNED role_envelope based on intent classification.

So the user's mandate to use runtime-profile.json instead of brain.json raises a question: the current runtime-profile.json also doesn't have a `current_agent` field. It has `role_envelope.primary.agent` which is the INTENT-based primary agent, not the actual running agent.

However, this is MUCH better than brain.json because:
1. It's deterministic (bash-generated, sha256-hashed)
2. It's not LLM-mutable
3. The `role_envelope.primary.agent` IS deterministic given the intent

The question for the blueprint is: should we extend gx-entry-guard.sh to accept a `--agent` parameter and write it as a `current_agent` field? Or should we use a different mechanism?

Actually, looking more carefully at the OpenCode platform, when an agent session starts, the agent name IS available. The `session.created` event has `properties.info` which should include agent info. And `context-injection.ts` already checks `state.current.agent === "hivefiver"` (we verified this in earlier sessions).

For the revised blueprint, the approach should be:
1. Fix 3 first (session isolation) — create session-scoped directories
2. During session creation, write a `session-profile.json` in the session-scoped directory that includes the agent name (deterministic, written once at session start)
3. Fix 1.5 (Schema Detox) — prune brain.json
4. Fix 1 (Decoupling) — hooks read `session-profile.json` from session-scoped directory for agent resolution
5. Fix 2 (Relational Staleness) — last

Now let me also note a critical gap: `runtime-profile.json` uses INTENT-BASED agent resolution (not SESSION-AGENT-BASED). It maps "what kind of work" to "which agent team", not "which agent is currently running". The profile says hiveminder is primary for build_new, but it doesn't know if the session was started AS hivefiver.

This is actually a design gap that supports the user's mandate even MORE strongly — we need a session-scoped profile that captures the ACTUAL running agent, not an intent-classified team composition.

Let me now draft the Revised Node 1 Blueprint v2.

## Key Finding from the Profile Pattern Investigation

The `runtime-profile.json` has a **design gap** that I must surface honestly:

| What runtime-profile.json HAS | What we NEED for decoupling |
|------|------|
| `role_envelope.primary.agent` = intent-classified team lead (e.g., "hiveminder" for `build_new`) | The **actual running agent** in this session (e.g., "hivefiver") |
| `intent` = work type classification (`build_new`, `fix_broken`, etc.) | Agent identity for hook routing |

The `gx-entry-guard.sh` script maps **work intent → agent team**, not **session → running agent**. So even the Profile Pattern needs extension to carry `current_agent` for hook decoupling.

However, this is still **vastly safer** than brain.json because:
1. It's bash-generated, not LLM-mutable
2. It's deterministic (sha256 hash)
3. It can be extended with a `current_agent` field written once at session creation

Combined with your mandate for **session-scoped state**, the solution becomes: write a **session-scoped profile** in `sessions/active/<session-id>/profile.json` that captures the actual running agent at session creation time.

# REVISED NODE 1 BLUEPRINT v2

## VETO ACKNOWLEDGMENT

The v1 Blueprint contained three fatal flaws caught by the Human Architect:

1. **Concurrency Paradox**: Proposed decoupling (Fix 1) before session isolation (Fix 3). A global `brain.json` cannot route agent-specific hooks when multiple sessions overwrite it concurrently.
2. **Toxic Data Trap**: Proposed `brain.json` for hard infrastructure routing. Audited `brain.json` shows: `role: ""`, voodoo metrics (`evidence_pressure: 364`), narrative monologues in hierarchy fields, and token-draining `cycle_log` blobs.
3. **Hallucination Engine**: `brain.json` is LLM-mutable state. Building deterministic infrastructure on it is building on quicksand.

**All three are accepted. The blueprint is rewritten from foundation up.**

---

## CORRECTED EXECUTION ORDER

```
Fix 3  (Session Isolation)     ← FOUNDATION — must exist before anything reads state
  ↓
Fix 1.5 (Schema Detox)         ← CLEAN THE DATA before routing on it
  ↓
Fix 1  (Dual-Injection Decouple) ← NOW safe to route — session-scoped, clean data
  ↓
Fix 2  (Relational Staleness)  ← LAST — scoring depends on clean state
```

**Rationale**: You cannot route hooks if you cannot isolate sessions. You cannot isolate sessions if the data they carry is poisoned. Fix the container → fix the contents → fix the routing → fix the scoring.

---

## FIX 3: SESSION-SCOPED STATE ISOLATION (Phases A–D)

### The Problem (Verified)

`paths.ts` (530 lines) defines all state paths as project-global:
- `state/brain.json` — ONE global file  
- `state/hierarchy.json` — ONE global file
- `state/todo.json` — ONE global file

Two concurrent sessions read/write the same files → cross-contamination.

The `sessions/` directory structure EXISTS in `paths.ts` (lines 66-71: `sessionsDir`, `activeDir`, `archiveDir`) but contains NO per-session state subdirectories. Current `sessions/active/` holds only a single `.md` file. The `sessions/manifest.json` is **empty** (`{"sessions": [], "active_stamp": null}`).

### The Architecture

```
.hivemind/
├── config.json                              # Project-level (shared, stable)
├── state/
│   ├── hierarchy.json                       # Project-level SOT (the tree)
│   └── schema-registry.json                 # Project-level schema registry
│
├── sessions/
│   ├── manifest.json                        # Session registry
│   ├── active/
│   │   └── <session-id>/                    # ← NEW: Per-session isolated state
│   │       ├── profile.json                 # Deterministic session profile (bash-generated)
│   │       ├── brain.json                   # Session-scoped runtime state
│   │       ├── todo.json                    # Session-scoped TODOs
│   │       ├── health-metrics.json          # Session-scoped health
│   │       ├── enforcement.json             # Session-scoped enforcement
│   │       ├── context-recovery.json        # Session-scoped recovery
│   │       └── cursor.json                  # Session's pointer into hierarchy.json
│   │
│   └── archive/                             # Completed sessions
```

**Key principle**: `hierarchy.json` stays project-level (it IS the shared tree). Everything else becomes session-scoped.

### Phase A: Add `getSessionPaths()` to `paths.ts` (Additive)

**Target**: `src/lib/paths.ts`

```typescript
// NEW interface
export interface SessionScopedPaths {
  sessionDir: string            // sessions/active/<session-id>/
  profile: string               // sessions/active/<session-id>/profile.json
  brain: string                 // sessions/active/<session-id>/brain.json  
  todo: string                  // sessions/active/<session-id>/todo.json
  healthMetrics: string         // sessions/active/<session-id>/health-metrics.json
  enforcement: string           // sessions/active/<session-id>/enforcement.json
  contextRecovery: string       // sessions/active/<session-id>/context-recovery.json
  cursor: string                // sessions/active/<session-id>/cursor.json
}

// NEW function
export function getSessionPaths(
  projectRoot: string,
  sessionId: string
): SessionScopedPaths {
  const base = getEffectivePaths(projectRoot)
  const sessionDir = join(base.activeDir, sessionId)
  return {
    sessionDir,
    profile: join(sessionDir, "profile.json"),
    brain: join(sessionDir, "brain.json"),
    todo: join(sessionDir, "todo.json"),
    healthMetrics: join(sessionDir, "health-metrics.json"),
    enforcement: join(sessionDir, "enforcement.json"),
    contextRecovery: join(sessionDir, "context-recovery.json"),
    cursor: join(sessionDir, "cursor.json"),
  }
}
```

**Blast radius**: 0 files affected. Pure addition. No existing code changes.

### Phase B: Create Session Directory on `session.created` Event

**Target**: `src/hooks/event-handler.ts` (line 180-182)

Currently:
```typescript
case "session.created":
  await log.info(`[event] session.created: ${(event as EventSessionCreated).properties.info.id}`)
  break
```

Becomes:
```typescript
case "session.created": {
  const sessionId = (event as EventSessionCreated).properties.info.id
  await log.info(`[event] session.created: ${sessionId}`)
  
  // Create session-scoped directory
  const sessionPaths = getSessionPaths(effectiveDir, sessionId)
  await mkdir(sessionPaths.sessionDir, { recursive: true })
  
  // Write deterministic session profile
  const agentName = (event as EventSessionCreated).properties.info.agent ?? "unknown"
  const profile = {
    session_id: sessionId,
    agent: agentName,
    created: new Date().toISOString(),
    created_epoch: Date.now(),
    source: "event-handler:session.created",
    deterministic: true
  }
  await writeFile(sessionPaths.profile, JSON.stringify(profile, null, 2))
  break
}
```

**Critical question to verify**: Does `EventSessionCreated.properties.info` include the agent name? This needs code-level verification. If not available from the event, we fall back to reading the OpenCode session API.

### Phase C: Copy Global State → Session State on First Access

When a hook first tries to read `brain.json` for a session, if the session-scoped copy doesn't exist, copy from global. This ensures backward compatibility.

**Implementation**: A `getSessionState()` utility that:
1. Check `sessions/active/<id>/brain.json` — if exists, read it
2. If not, copy `state/brain.json` → `sessions/active/<id>/brain.json`, then read
3. Return the session-scoped state

### Phase D: Switch Hooks to Prefer Session-Scoped Paths with Global Fallback

All hooks that currently read from `state/brain.json` switch to:
```typescript
const brainPath = sessionId 
  ? getSessionPaths(root, sessionId).brain 
  : paths.brain  // global fallback
```

**We stop at Phase D.** No deprecation, no breaking changes. Global fallback ensures backward compatibility.

## FIX 1.5: SCHEMA DETOX & LINEAGE ENFORCEMENT

### The Problem (Verified from BrainState Investigation)

The BrainState schema (`src/schemas/brain-state.ts`) contains:

**A. Orphan Fields (WRITE-ONLY — never read by any hook):**

| Field | Written By | Read By | Verdict |
|-------|-----------|---------|---------|
| `metrics.ratings` | `brain-state.ts:467-483` | **NOBODY** | ⚠️ PRUNE |
| `memory_governance.classified_counts` | `messages-transform.ts:445-461` | **NOBODY** | ⚠️ PRUNE |
| `memory_governance.temporary_exports_*` | `brain-state.ts:602-621` | **NOBODY** | ⚠️ PRUNE |
| `complexity_nudge_shown` | `brain-state.ts:485-497` | **NOBODY** | ⚠️ PRUNE |
| `last_commit_suggestion_turn` | `brain-state.ts:499-504` | **NOBODY** | ⚠️ PRUNE |

**B. Voodoo Metrics (arbitrary counters with no deterministic meaning):**

| Field | Current Value | What It Measures | Problem |
|-------|--------------|-----------------|---------|
| `evidence_pressure` | 364 | Incremented when evidence-related keywords detected | No ceiling, no action threshold, pure noise |
| `ignored` | 179 | Incremented when governance message not acknowledged | "Acknowledged" is never actually set to true |
| `write_without_read_count` | 0 | Writes without prior reads | Already validated by CQRS queue |
| `out_of_order` | 0 | Governance step ordering violations | Dead — never triggered |

**C. Token Drain (cycle_log):**

`cycle_log` (schema lines 73-84) stores `CycleLogEntry[]` where each entry has `output_excerpt: string` — first 500 chars of tool output. With 183 tool calls, that's ~90K characters of raw text hoarded in a JSON file, injected into context every turn by `messages-transform.ts:658`.

**D. Narrative Hierarchy (no lineage IDs):**

Current `hierarchy` fields contain:
```
"trajectory": "THE-FRAMEWORK-TEST-ITSELF: Master-planning refactoring via timeline documents..."
"tactic": "Governance adjustment: stop using gsd-* agents..."  
"action": "Deep research into GSD asset chaining pattern..."
```

Should contain:
```
"trajectory": "PROJ-001"        → maps to .hivemind/graph/project/project.json
"tactic": "PHASE-02"           → maps to .hivemind/graph/plans/PHASE-02.json
"action": "TASK-04"            → maps to .hivemind/graph/tasks/TASK-04.json
```

### The Detox Plan

**Step 1: Prune Orphan Fields from Schema**

Remove from `BrainState` interface and `BRAIN_STATE_FIELD_CLASSIFICATION`:
- `metrics.ratings` + `SelfRating` type
- `memory_governance.classified_counts`
- `memory_governance.temporary_exports_consolidated`
- `memory_governance.temporary_exports_purged`
- `complexity_nudge_shown`
- `last_commit_suggestion_turn`

Remove corresponding mutation methods from `brain-state.ts` (e.g., `addSelfRating`, `updateComplexityNudge`).

**Step 2: Kill Voodoo Metrics**

Replace `GovernanceCounters` (from `src/lib/detection.ts:87-95`) with:
```typescript
interface GovernanceCounters {
  compaction: number          // KEEP — deterministic (actual compaction events)
  drift: number               // KEEP — derived from git/hierarchy comparison
  // REMOVED: evidence_pressure, ignored, out_of_order, acknowledged, prerequisites_completed
}
```

Update `soft-governance.ts` to stop incrementing dead counters.

**Step 3: Cap or Kill cycle_log**

Two options:
- **Option A (Cap)**: Hard limit `cycle_log` to last 5 entries (instead of unbounded). Older entries are dropped on write.
- **Option B (Kill)**: Remove `cycle_log` entirely. The data it stores is already available via OpenCode's native session history.

**Recommendation**: Option A (Cap to 5). Some consumers use it for boundary detection (`messages-transform.ts:658`). Capping limits token drain without breaking consumers.

**Step 4: Enforce Lineage IDs in Hierarchy**

Modify `HierarchyState` schema (`src/schemas/hierarchy.ts:12-16`):
```typescript
interface HierarchyState {
  trajectory: string    // MUST be a lineage ID (e.g., "PROJ-001") or empty string
  tactic: string        // MUST be a lineage ID (e.g., "PHASE-02") or empty string  
  action: string        // MUST be a lineage ID (e.g., "TASK-04") or empty string
}
```

Add a validation function:
```typescript
const LINEAGE_ID_PATTERN = /^[A-Z]+-\d+$/
export function validateHierarchyLineage(h: HierarchyState): string[] {
  const errors: string[] = []
  for (const [field, value] of Object.entries(h)) {
    if (value && !LINEAGE_ID_PATTERN.test(value) && value !== "") {
      errors.push(`${field}: "${value.slice(0, 50)}..." is not a lineage ID`)
    }
  }
  return errors
}
```

**Gap Registration**: When a hierarchy field cannot be linked to a planning artifact, it registers as:
```json
{ "trajectory": "GAP:unlinked", "tactic": "", "action": "" }
```

This explicitly marks the gap as a returning point rather than hallucinating fake continuity.

## FIX 1: DUAL-INJECTION DECOUPLING (Agent-Domain Routing)

### The Problem (unchanged from v1)

Two injection systems fire every turn, unaware of each other. Both read `hierarchy.json`. Both inject hierarchy data. Different formats → contradictory context.

### The Resolution Method: Session-Scoped Profile (NOT brain.json)

**Previous (VETOED)**: Read `state.session.agent` from `brain.json`  
**New (MANDATED)**: Read `profile.json` from session-scoped directory

After Fix 3 runs, each session has:
```
sessions/active/<session-id>/profile.json
```

```json
{
  "session_id": "abc-123",
  "agent": "hivefiver",
  "created": "2026-03-04T10:00:00Z",
  "created_epoch": 1709546400,
  "source": "event-handler:session.created",
  "deterministic": true
}
```

This file is:
- ✅ Written ONCE at session creation (not LLM-mutable)
- ✅ Written by TypeScript event handler (deterministic)
- ✅ Session-scoped (no cross-contamination)
- ✅ Contains the actual running agent name
- ✅ Has `deterministic: true` flag for self-documentation

### Guard Implementation

**META_BUILDER_AGENTS** constant (shared):
```typescript
const META_BUILDER_AGENTS = ["hivefiver"] as const
```

**1A. `context-injection.ts` — System 1 Guard:**
```typescript
// Read session-scoped profile for agent identity
const sessionProfile = readSessionProfile(workdir, sessionId)
const currentAgent = sessionProfile?.agent ?? "unknown"

// System 1 ONLY fires for meta-builder agents
if (!META_BUILDER_AGENTS.includes(currentAgent)) {
  return  // Skip injection for product agents
}
```

**1B. `session-lifecycle.ts` — System 2 Guard:**
```typescript
// Read session-scoped profile for agent identity  
const sessionProfile = readSessionProfile(effectiveDir, input.sessionID)
const currentAgent = sessionProfile?.agent ?? "unknown"

// System 2 ONLY fires for product agents (inverse guard)
if (META_BUILDER_AGENTS.includes(currentAgent)) {
  return  // Skip injection for meta-builder agents
}
```

**1C. `messages-transform.ts` — Same inverse pattern as 1B**

**Fail-Open Safety**: If `profile.json` doesn't exist or `agent` is `"unknown"`, BOTH systems fire (preserving current behavior). This means old sessions without session-scoped directories still work.

## FIX 2: RELATIONAL STALENESS (Kill Wall-Clock)

### The Problem (unchanged from v1)

`gx-signal-hierarchy-freshness.sh` lines 89-97:
```bash
age_minutes=$((age_seconds / 60))
score=$((100 - (age_minutes * decay_rate)))
```

Score hits ZERO after 10 minutes. Coffee break = "CRITICAL DRIFT."

### The Fix (unchanged concept, deferred to last)

Replace wall-clock with three relational signals:
- **Git Drift (0-40 pts)**: How many commits since hierarchy last updated
- **Row-Chain Continuity (0-35 pts)**: Are hierarchy IDs valid lineage references
- **Session Continuity (0-25 pts)**: Does the session-scoped profile match active hierarchy

**Why last**: This script reads `hierarchy.json` and `health-metrics.json`. After Fix 3, those reads must respect session-scoped paths. After Fix 1.5, hierarchy fields contain lineage IDs that row-chain validation can actually check. Running this fix last means it operates on clean infrastructure.

## User

HE AUTOPSY OF BLUEPRINT v2 (THE HIDDEN TRAPS)
1. The "Global Copy" Infection Vector (Fix 3, Phase C)

What it proposed: If a session starts and doesn't have a scoped brain.json, copy the global state/brain.json into the new session.

Why it’s lethal: The entire reason for this refactor is that the global state is a toxic garbage fire. If a clean session starts by importing the global poison into its isolated room, you have achieved absolutely nothing. Isolation must mean a clean slate.

2. The cycle_log Compromise (Question 2)

What it proposed: Capping cycle_log to 5 entries instead of killing it, because messages-transform.ts relies on it.

Why it’s lethal: 5 entries of 500 characters is still 2,500 characters of useless raw terminal text (output_excerpt) bleeding into the prompt every turn, diluting the context window.

The Fix: Schema Lobotomy. We don't kill the array, we kill the text blob. We remove the output_excerpt string completely. The log becomes pure telemetry: { timestamp, tool, failure_detected }. This keeps the boundary logic intact without poisoning the prompt with historical stdout.

3. The Global mtime Fallacy (Fix 2)

What it proposed: Check git drift by comparing uncommitted changes to the mtime (modified time) of the global hierarchy.json.

Why it’s lethal: hierarchy.json is a shared tree. If Session A (Frontend) updates the hierarchy at 10:00 AM, the file's mtime becomes 10:00 AM. If Session B (Backend) checks its drift at 10:01 AM, it will calculate drift based on Session A's timestamp, completely blinding Session B to its own staleness!

The Fix: Git drift must be calculated against the last_sync timestamp of the specific SOT planning artifact (the markdown file in .hivemind/plans/) that the session's cursor is tied to, NOT the global hierarchy file. (Also, stat -f %m is macOS-only and will break on Linux/WSL).

4. The Brittle Regex Breakage (Fix 1.5, Step 4)

What it proposed: Enforcing lineage IDs with /^[A-Z]+-\d+$/ (e.g., PROJ-001).

Why it’s lethal: In your codebase (e.g., PLAN-MATERIALIZE-CONTRACT-2026-03-03.md), atomic plans use IDs like META01-SUB01-ATOMIC01. Furthermore, existing hierarchy nodes use formats like traj/gx-pack or action/decision-log. The AI's regex will immediately throw validation errors on valid framework artifacts and hard-block all planning stages. <<<<<<>>>>> HAVE YOUR OWN REASONING HARD AND RATIOANLE IF I AM NOT CORRECT READY TO CHALLENGE ME AT ALL COST , IF TRUE THEN "SYSTEM DIRECTIVE: BLUEPRINT APPROVED WITH MECHANICAL CAVEATS

Your Revised Node 1 Blueprint v2 is structurally excellent. The `cursor.json` pattern to decouple the global tree from session-local pointers is exactly the enterprise-grade architecture required to solve the concurrency problem. 

I am approving the Blueprint for execution, but as the Principal Architect, I have audited your specific implementation logic and found four lethal logic bombs. You will apply the following **Hardness Amendments** immediately as you begin execution.

## THE HARDNESS AMENDMENTS:

### 1. VETO: "Copy Global State to Session" (Fix 3, Phase C)
**DO NOT copy the global `brain.json` into new sessions.** The global state is a toxic garbage fire. If you copy it, you copy the poison into the clean room.
**Correction:** If a session-scoped `brain.json` does not exist, initialize a **fresh, empty state**. If legacy scripts break because they look for global state, let them break. We will fix them in later nodes. Isolation is absolute.

### 2. VETO: Restrictive Lineage Regex (Fix 1.5, Step 4)
**DO NOT use `/^[A-Z]+-\d+$/`.** Look at our actual test files and SOTs: we use IDs like `traj/gx-pack`, `action/decision-log`, and `META01-SUB01-ATOMIC01`. Your regex will crash the system immediately.
**Correction:** Change the validation rule to simply ensure it is a programmatic ID, not a narrative. Rule: **"Must be under 64 characters, and must not contain spaces or newline characters."** Narrative text fails this; valid IDs pass this. Keep it simple.

### 3. VETO: Global `mtime` for Git Drift (Fix 2)
**DO NOT use the `mtime` of the global `hierarchy.json`.** Because it is a shared file, Session A updating the tree will reset the drift timer for Session B, blinding Session B to its own staleness. Furthermore, `stat -f %m` is macOS-only.
**Correction:** Git drift must be calculated against the `last_sync` timestamp of the *specific SOT planning artifact* (e.g., `.hivemind/plans/META01.md`) that the session's cursor points to. Use existing cross-platform `stat` wrappers found in the codebase.

## MY CHALLENGE ASSESSMENT — All Four Findings Examined

I will not be sycophantic. Let me reason through each finding honestly.

---

### Finding 1: "Global Copy" Infection Vector — **YOU ARE CORRECT. I concede.**

My Phase C proposed: "If session-scoped brain.json doesn't exist, copy from global." This is logically self-defeating. The entire premise of this refactor is that `brain.json` contains `evidence_pressure: 364`, narrative monologues in hierarchy, and token-draining cycle_log blobs. Copying that into an "isolated" session directory is copying the disease into the quarantine ward. 

**My error**: I was optimizing for backward compatibility when I should have been optimizing for correctness. A fresh session deserves a fresh state. If legacy scripts break, they surface the coupling they were hiding.

**Amendment accepted: Clean-slate initialization. No global copy.**

---

### Finding 2: cycle_log Lobotomy — **YOU ARE CORRECT. Your solution is superior to mine.**

I proposed capping to 5 entries. You proposed killing `output_excerpt` but keeping the signal structure. Your approach is better for two reasons:

1. **My cap still poisons**: 5 × 500 chars = 2,500 chars of raw terminal output injected every turn. That's ~600 tokens of noise per turn for zero decision value.
2. **Your lobotomy preserves function**: `messages-transform.ts:658` uses cycle_log for session boundary detection. It needs `timestamp` and `tool` to detect boundaries — it does NOT need the stdout text to make that determination. `{ timestamp, tool, failure_detected, failure_keywords }` gives the boundary detector everything it needs with ~50 chars per entry instead of ~500.

**Amendment accepted: Kill `output_excerpt`, keep telemetry skeleton.**

---

### Finding 3: Global mtime Fallacy — **YOU ARE CORRECT. I missed a concurrency bug I was specifically trying to fix.**

This is embarrassing because the ENTIRE premise of this blueprint is solving multi-session concurrency, and I introduced a concurrency bug in my own fix. If Session A updates `hierarchy.json` at 10:00 AM, Session B checking drift at 10:01 sees "1 minute old = fresh!" even though Session B's own planning artifacts haven't been touched in 3 hours.

**Additionally**: `stat -f %m` is macOS-only. I should have caught this — the codebase runs on Linux/WSL too. Cross-platform stat handling is basic engineering.

**Your fix is architecturally sound**: Drift must be relative to the specific SOT artifact the session's `cursor.json` points to, not the shared tree. This is exactly what the cursor pattern was designed for.

**Amendment accepted: Per-cursor-artifact drift, not global mtime.**

---

### Finding 4: Brittle Regex — **YOU ARE CORRECT. My regex would have hard-blocked the system.**

I proposed `/^[A-Z]+-\d+$/` to validate lineage IDs. Let me test it against actual IDs from the codebase:

| Actual ID | My Regex | Result |
|-----------|----------|--------|
| `traj/gx-pack` | ❌ FAIL | Has `/`, lowercase |
| `action/decision-log` | ❌ FAIL | Has `/`, lowercase, hyphen |
| `META01-SUB01-ATOMIC01` | ❌ FAIL | Multiple segments |
| `PLAN-MATERIALIZE-CONTRACT-2026-03-03` | ❌ FAIL | Has date format |
| `PHASE-02` | ✅ PASS | Only format that works |

4 out of 5 valid IDs rejected. My regex would crash planning stages on the first `declare_intent` call.

Your rule — "under 64 characters, no spaces, no newlines" — is pragmatic and correct. Narrative text (`"THE-FRAMEWORK-TEST-ITSELF: Master-planning refactoring via timeline documents..."`) contains spaces. Programmatic IDs don't. Simple, unbreakable.

**Amendment accepted: Length + no-whitespace validation, not rigid regex.**

---

## VERDICT: ALL FOUR FINDINGS CORRECT

I have no challenges. All four are genuine logic bombs that would have detonated during implementation. The Blueprint v2 is approved with all Hardness Amendments applied.
